The Heart as the Locus of Iman
Nasafi argues that iman is located in the heart, not the tongue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Nasafi argues that iman is seated in the heart, using practical examples and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Faith is not what you say, but what your heart affirms.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi begins by establishing that iman is fundamentally an affair of the heart. He observes that verbal confession is often impossible—during prayer, in the lavatory—yet the obligation of iman remains, proving it is not dependent on the tongue. He then cites the Quranic verse about coercion to show that the heart's tranquility in iman overrides forced utterance. This lesson walks through those arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage once to get a feel for Nasafi's concise style. Then read the literal translation carefully.
Notice the repeated phrase 'yuhaqqiquhu' indicating verification.
2
Identify the main arguments
Find the two key proofs: (1) the impossibility of verbal confession in certain states, and (2) the Quranic verse about coercion (16:106). Understand how each supports the heart as the locus of iman.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that the heart is the seat of iman and that kufr of the heart prevents tongue's speech from being iman. Consider why this matters for understanding faith.
This directly refutes those who define iman solely by outward confession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الإيمان دين والأديان تعتقد والاعتقادات بالقلوب.
يحققه أن ارتفاع فعل الإيمان عن الممتحنين محال، وتمر عامة الأوقات ولا توجد الشهادة باللسان بل من الأحوال ما ينهي المرء فيه أن يقول آمنت بالكتب والنبيين والبعث ونحو ذلك كما في الصلوات وكما في حال كونه في الكنيف، وكما في حال خروج البول والغائط منه ومحال ارتفاع فرض الإيمان أو النهي عنه ما دام التكليف باقيًا أو القول بكراهيته حال وجود العبادة التي لا صحة لها إلا به، وكل ذلك يدل على أن الإيمان في الحقيقة هو التصديق، والذي يؤيد هذا كله قوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَنُ بِالْإِيمَن ) لم يجعل لهم كفرًا باللسان إذا لم يكن عبارة عن القلب ومنع ذلك أن يكون كفرًا بإيمان القلب فثبت أن القلب هو موضع الإيمان وبه يستدل أن كفر القلب يمنع قول اللسان من أن يكون إيمانًا، والله الموفق.
[المعرفة لا تكفي بل لابد من تصديق القلب]
ثم بالقلب يكون التصديق لما مر أن الإيمان يكون بالقلب والإيمان هو التصديق، وليست المعرفة الخالية عن التصديق إيمانًا كما ظن جهم وجماعة أن الإيمان هو المعرفة لما أن الإيمان هو التصديق ثم ضد الإيمان هو الكفر، والكفر هو التكذيب والتكذيب ينافي التصديق لا المعرفة إذ ما يضادها النكرة والجهالة، وليس كل من جهل حقا يكذب به.
يحققه أن الإيمان بجميع الأنبياء والرسل وبجميع الكتب وجميع الملائكة ثابت وهو التصديق، والمعرفة بأعيانهم منعدمة، وأهل العناد كانوا يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم وكانوا يكتمون الحق وهم يعلمون، ولم يثبت لهم الإيمان بتلك المعرفة لانعدام التصديق وثبوت ما يضاده وهو التكذيب، والله الموفق.
He verifies that iman is a religion, and religions are believed, and beliefs are in hearts. He verifies that the absence of the act of iman from those under obligation is impossible. Most times pass and the testimony by the tongue does not occur, rather there are states in which a person is prevented from saying 'I believe in the books, the prophets, the resurrection,' and similar things, as in prayers, and as when he is in the latrine, and as when he is passing urine or stool. It is impossible for the obligation of iman or the prohibition of it to be lifted as long as obligation remains, or to say that it is disliked in a state where there is an act of worship that is only valid through it. All of this indicates that iman in reality is tasdiq (affirmation). Supporting all this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Except one who is forced while his heart is tranquil in iman.' He did not count their speech as kufr when it did not express the heart, and prevented that from being kufr because of the heart's iman. So it is established that the heart is the locus of iman, and by this it is inferred that kufr of the heart prevents the saying of the tongue from being iman. And Allah is the grantor of success. [Knowledge is not sufficient; rather affirmation of the heart is necessary] Then by the heart is affirmation, because it has been mentioned that iman is by the heart and iman is tasdiq. Knowledge devoid of tasdiq is not iman, as Jahm and a group thought that iman is ma'rifa (knowledge). For iman is tasdiq, and the opposite of iman is kufr, and kufr is takdhib (denial). Takdhib contradicts tasdiq, not ma'rifa, for its opposite is nukra (denial) and jahala (ignorance). Not everyone who is ignorant of a truth denies it. He verifies that iman in all prophets and messengers, all books, and all angels is established, and it is tasdiq, while ma'rifa of their individual identities is absent. The obstinate knew him as they knew their sons, and they concealed the truth while they knew it, but iman was not established for them by that knowledge due to the absence of tasdiq and the presence of its opposite, takdhib. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1092

Commentary
This is a definitional and argumentative passage in which Imam al-Nasafi establishes that iman (faith) is essentially tasdiq (affirmation) by the heart, not merely ma'rifa (knowledge). He begins by arguing that iman is a matter of belief seated in the heart, supporting this with the observation that verbal confession is often impossible (e.g., during prayer, in the lavatory), yet the obligation of iman remains—showing iman is not dependent on utterance. He then cites the Quranic verse (16:106) about coercion, where the heart's tranquility in iman prevents the forced utterance from being kufr, establishing that the heart is the true locus of iman. Nasafi refutes Jahm's view equating iman with ma'rifa, noting that iman's opposite is kufr (denial), not ignorance, and denial contradicts tasdiq, not knowledge. Finally, he proves that knowledge alone is insufficient: the obstinate (like Abu Jahl) knew the Prophet but denied him, so they had no iman despite having ma'rifa. The passage thus distinguishes tasdiq as the essence of iman.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
القلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does Nasafi use to argue that iman is not merely verbal confession?
A) The Quran says iman is in the heart.
B) People in the lavatory cannot utter the shahada yet they remain believers.
C) The Prophet said iman is hidden.
D) Knowledge is sufficient for iman.

Key Takeaway
Iman is essentially affirmation of the heart, not mere verbal confession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada with your tongue, do you ever sense a gap between your lips and your heart? What would it take to close that gap today?
?
Think of a moment when you felt pressured to say something against your faith—how did your heart respond? Did that moment reveal the true state of your iman?
?
If iman is truly in the heart, what is one concrete step you will take this week to strengthen your inner conviction, not merely your outward practice?

Refuting the View that Iman is Merely Knowledge
Nasafi refutes Jahm's equation of iman with ma'rifa using logical and historical proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why knowledge (ma'rifa) alone does not constitute iman, and why affirmation (tasdiq) is essential, as argued by Nasafi against Jahm.

Core Idea
Knowing the truth is not enough—you must affirm it with your heart.

Imam al-Nasafi now directly refutes the position of Jahm ibn Safwan and others who claimed that iman is simply knowledge of Allah. Nasafi shows that the opposite of iman is kufr, which means denial (takdhib), not ignorance. Denial contradicts affirmation (tasdiq), not knowledge. He illustrates this with the example of the obstinate people of Mecca who knew the Prophet but denied him—they had ma'rifa but no iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Focus on the section beginning with 'ثم بالقلب يكون التصديق'. Read it alongside the translation.
Notice the logical relationship between iman, tasdiq, kufr, and takdhib.
2
Understand the logical argument
Nasafi says: iman = tasdiq, so its opposite (kufr) must be takdhib. Takdhib contradicts tasdiq, not ma'rifa. Therefore, if iman were ma'rifa, its opposite would be ignorance, not denial. But we know kufr is denial, not mere ignorance.
This is a key semantic argument.
3
Examine the historical example
The obstinate (like Abu Jahl) knew the Prophet intimately but denied him. They had ma'rifa but no iman because they lacked tasdiq and instead had takdhib.
This proves that ma'rifa without tasdiq is insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الإيمان دين والأديان تعتقد والاعتقادات بالقلوب.
يحققه أن ارتفاع فعل الإيمان عن الممتحنين محال، وتمر عامة الأوقات ولا توجد الشهادة باللسان بل من الأحوال ما ينهي المرء فيه أن يقول آمنت بالكتب والنبيين والبعث ونحو ذلك كما في الصلوات وكما في حال كونه في الكنيف، وكما في حال خروج البول والغائط منه ومحال ارتفاع فرض الإيمان أو النهي عنه ما دام التكليف باقيًا أو القول بكراهيته حال وجود العبادة التي لا صحة لها إلا به، وكل ذلك يدل على أن الإيمان في الحقيقة هو التصديق، والذي يؤيد هذا كله قوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَنُ بِالْإِيمَن ) لم يجعل لهم كفرًا باللسان إذا لم يكن عبارة عن القلب ومنع ذلك أن يكون كفرًا بإيمان القلب فثبت أن القلب هو موضع الإيمان وبه يستدل أن كفر القلب يمنع قول اللسان من أن يكون إيمانًا، والله الموفق.
[المعرفة لا تكفي بل لابد من تصديق القلب]
ثم بالقلب يكون التصديق لما مر أن الإيمان يكون بالقلب والإيمان هو التصديق، وليست المعرفة الخالية عن التصديق إيمانًا كما ظن جهم وجماعة أن الإيمان هو المعرفة لما أن الإيمان هو التصديق ثم ضد الإيمان هو الكفر، والكفر هو التكذيب والتكذيب ينافي التصديق لا المعرفة إذ ما يضادها النكرة والجهالة، وليس كل من جهل حقا يكذب به.
يحققه أن الإيمان بجميع الأنبياء والرسل وبجميع الكتب وجميع الملائكة ثابت وهو التصديق، والمعرفة بأعيانهم منعدمة، وأهل العناد كانوا يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم وكانوا يكتمون الحق وهم يعلمون، ولم يثبت لهم الإيمان بتلك المعرفة لانعدام التصديق وثبوت ما يضاده وهو التكذيب، والله الموفق.
He verifies that iman is a religion, and religions are believed, and beliefs are in hearts. He verifies that the absence of the act of iman from those under obligation is impossible. Most times pass and the testimony by the tongue does not occur, rather there are states in which a person is prevented from saying 'I believe in the books, the prophets, the resurrection,' and similar things, as in prayers, and as when he is in the latrine, and as when he is passing urine or stool. It is impossible for the obligation of iman or the prohibition of it to be lifted as long as obligation remains, or to say that it is disliked in a state where there is an act of worship that is only valid through it. All of this indicates that iman in reality is tasdiq (affirmation). Supporting all this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Except one who is forced while his heart is tranquil in iman.' He did not count their speech as kufr when it did not express the heart, and prevented that from being kufr because of the heart's iman. So it is established that the heart is the locus of iman, and by this it is inferred that kufr of the heart prevents the saying of the tongue from being iman. And Allah is the grantor of success. [Knowledge is not sufficient; rather affirmation of the heart is necessary] Then by the heart is affirmation, because it has been mentioned that iman is by the heart and iman is tasdiq. Knowledge devoid of tasdiq is not iman, as Jahm and a group thought that iman is ma'rifa (knowledge). For iman is tasdiq, and the opposite of iman is kufr, and kufr is takdhib (denial). Takdhib contradicts tasdiq, not ma'rifa, for its opposite is nukra (denial) and jahala (ignorance). Not everyone who is ignorant of a truth denies it. He verifies that iman in all prophets and messengers, all books, and all angels is established, and it is tasdiq, while ma'rifa of their individual identities is absent. The obstinate knew him as they knew their sons, and they concealed the truth while they knew it, but iman was not established for them by that knowledge due to the absence of tasdiq and the presence of its opposite, takdhib. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1092

Commentary
This is a definitional and argumentative passage in which Imam al-Nasafi establishes that iman (faith) is essentially tasdiq (affirmation) by the heart, not merely ma'rifa (knowledge). He begins by arguing that iman is a matter of belief seated in the heart, supporting this with the observation that verbal confession is often impossible (e.g., during prayer, in the lavatory), yet the obligation of iman remains—showing iman is not dependent on utterance. He then cites the Quranic verse (16:106) about coercion, where the heart's tranquility in iman prevents the forced utterance from being kufr, establishing that the heart is the true locus of iman. Nasafi refutes Jahm's view equating iman with ma'rifa, noting that iman's opposite is kufr (denial), not ignorance, and denial contradicts tasdiq, not knowledge. Finally, he proves that knowledge alone is insufficient: the obstinate (like Abu Jahl) knew the Prophet but denied him, so they had no iman despite having ma'rifa. The passage thus distinguishes tasdiq as the essence of iman.

Key Terms
التصديق
المعرفة
الكفر
التكذيب
جهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman is simply intellectual knowledge of Allah and His commands.
Correction: Nasafi shows that knowledge without heartfelt affirmation (tasdiq) is not iman, as seen in the obstinate who knew the truth but denied it.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi use to prove that knowledge (ma'rifa) alone is not iman?
A) The Quran says iman is in the heart.
B) The obstinate knew the Prophet but denied him.
C) The Prophet said knowledge is not faith.
D) Iman requires both knowledge and action.

Key Takeaway
Iman is not mere knowledge but heartfelt affirmation; denial contradicts affirmation, not knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there a truth about Allah, the Prophet, or the Hereafter that you know intellectually but have not truly affirmed in your heart? What would it take for you to move from knowledge to tasdiq today?
?
Think of an area where your actions contradict what you know – are you, like the obstinate, denying with your deeds even while knowing the truth? Will you confess this denial and seek heartfelt affirmation?
?
If your iman were tested by the standard of tasdiq – not just information – would it stand firm? What one specific belief do you need to affirm more deeply starting now?

Iman as Tasdiq Does Not Increase or Decrease in Essence
Nasafi presents a logical argument that iman's essence is fixed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's logical argument that iman, being tasdiq (affirmation), is indivisible and therefore cannot increase or decrease in its essence.

Core Idea
Iman is tasdiq; it either exists or it doesn't—no degrees in its essence.

Nasafi begins by establishing the nature of iman as tasdiq, a single affirmation. He then applies a logical rule: anything that does not increase can only decrease by ceasing to exist, and increase only by adding another like it. Since acts of obedience are not additional affirmations of the same kind, they cannot increase iman's essence. This passage lays the groundwork for understanding why iman's essence is constant.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, noticing the logical flow from definition to conclusion. Then read the translation to grasp the argument.
Focus on the terms 'لا يتزايد' and 'لا نقصان'.
2
Identify the major premise
Identify the statement that iman (tasdiq) is something that does not increase. Ask why Nasafi says this.
Tasdiq is a single act of affirmation; it cannot be divided or increased.
3
Understand the condition for increase and decrease
Note the condition: what does not increase can only decrease by nonexistence, and increase only by adding another like it. Apply this to iman.
4
Draw the conclusion
Conclude that acts of obedience and sins do not affect the essence of iman. Understand that this is a logical necessity from the definition.
This will be contrasted with increase in light in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان الإيمان هو التصديق وهو في نفسه مما لا يتزايد وما لا يتزايد فلا نقصان له إلا بالعدم ولا زيادة عليه إلا بانضمام مثله إليه، فلا زيادة إذا للإيمان بانضمام الطاعات إليه، ولا نقصان بارتكاب المعاصي، إذ التصديق في الحالين على ما كان قبلهما فكان تأويل ما ورد من الزيادة في الإيمان على ما روى عن أبي حنيفة - رحمه الله - أنهم كانوا آمنوا في الجملة ثم يأتي فرض بعد فرض فيؤمن بكل فرض جاء فيزداد إيمانه بالتفسير مع إيمانه بالجملة وإن كان بالجملة في التحقيق إيمان به، وقد روى عن ابن عباس - رضي الله عنهما - هذا التأويل أيضا وكذا الثبات على الإيمان والدوام عليه زيادة عليه في كل ساعة إذ يوجد في كل ساعة مثل ما انعدم في الأولى كما يوجد درهم ثم يزداد عليه في كل ساعة درهم إلا أن تلك الزيادة في نفسه إذ هو غير محتمل للتجزؤ، ويحتمل الزيادة عليه أن يزداد نوره وضياؤه في القلوب بالأعمال الصاحة وينتقص ذلك بالمعاصي إذ الإيمان له ضياء ونور على ما قال تعالى: ﴿ يُرِيدُونَ لِيُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْرَهِهِمْ ) وقال تعالى: أَفَمَن شَرَحَ اللهُ صَدْرَهُ لِلإِسْلَامِ فَهُوَ عَلَى نُورٍ مِّن رَّبِّهِ ) فأما هو في ذاته فلا
And since iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and it is in itself something that does not increase, and what does not increase has no decrease except by nonexistence, and no increase except by adding another like it to it. Thus there is no increase for iman by adding acts of obedience to it, nor decrease by committing sins, for tasdiq in both states remains as it was before. So the interpretation of what has been reported about increase in iman is as narrated from Abu Hanifa—may Allah have mercy on him—that they believed in general, then obligation after obligation came, so they believed in each obligation that came, so his iman increased in detail along with his iman in general, even though in reality the general iman was already iman in it. This interpretation has also been narrated from Ibn Abbas—may Allah be pleased with them both. Likewise, persistence in iman and continuity upon it is an increase upon it every hour, for in every hour there exists what was absent in the first, just as a dirham exists then another dirham is added to it every hour, except that such increase is (imagined) in itself, for it is not susceptible to partitioning. However, it is possible for an increase to occur in its light and radiance in the hearts through righteous deeds, and that decreases through sins, for iman has illumination and light, as Allah Most High said: 'They desire to extinguish the light of Allah with their mouths' and He said: 'Is he whose breast Allah has expanded for Islam, so he is upon a light from his Lord?' As for it in itself, it does not (increase or decrease).
Source pages p. 1093

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about the nature of iman: it does not increase or decrease in its essence. Nasafi states that since iman is tasdiq (affirmation), which is a single, indivisible act, it cannot admit of increase or decrease in itself. Any increase would require adding another like it, but that would mean multiple affirmations, not increase of the same affirmation. Acts of obedience do not add to the essence of iman, nor do sins subtract from it. The reported increase in iman is interpreted in two ways: first, as increase in detail (tafsir) after believing in general (ijmal), as narrated from Abu Hanifa and Ibn Abbas; second, as an increase in the light and radiance of iman in the heart through good deeds, which can also decrease through sins. This light is distinct from the essence of iman. The verses about 'light of Allah' and 'light from his Lord' are cited to support this distinction. The passage concludes by implying that the essence of iman itself does not change.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الزيادة
النقصان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that iman itself increases with good deeds and decreases with sins.
Correction: Nasafi argues that iman's essence (tasdiq) does not change; only its light or radiance may increase or decrease.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does iman not increase by adding acts of obedience?
A) Because acts of obedience are not required for iman.
B) Because iman is tasdiq, and adding acts does not add another affirmation like it.
C) Because iman already includes all acts of obedience.
D) Because iman decreases when one disobeys.

Key Takeaway
Iman as tasdiq is indivisible; its essence neither increases with good deeds nor decreases with sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Since iman as tasdiq is either fully present or absent, are you certain that you truly affirm Allah in your heart? If you were asked today, 'Do you really believe?', would your answer be an unshakable 'yes'—or is there any doubt? What would it take for you to move from uncertainty to full conviction?
?
If sins do not decrease the essence of your iman, do you feel less urgency to avoid them? Does this teaching make you complacent, or does it rather free you to focus on the quality of your affirmation? Examine your heart: are you using this truth as an excuse for negligence, or as a foundation for sincere devotion?
?
The passage says acts of obedience do not increase iman. Does your spiritual life reflect that you value the fruit of faith over the quantity of deeds? Is your prayer, charity, and worship merely a habit, or a genuine expression of the tasdiq that is already complete? What needs to change in your intention today?

Increase in Iman: Detail, Persistence, and Light
Nasafi interprets reported increases in iman as increase in detail, persistence, or light, not essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how reported increases in iman are interpreted as going from general to detailed belief, persistence in faith, and increase in light or radiance, not in essence.

Core Idea
Reported increase in iman means more detailed knowledge or brighter light, not a stronger affirmation.

Having established that iman's essence does not change, Nasafi now addresses prophetic reports that mention 'increase in iman.' He presents two interpretations from Abu Hanifa and Ibn Abbas: the shift from general (ijmal) to detailed (tafsir) belief, and the idea of persistence as continuous renewal. He then introduces a third explanation: increase in the light of iman in the heart through good deeds, citing Quranic verses. This passage bridges scriptural texts and rational theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on interpretations
Read the Arabic and translation, noticing how Nasafi transitions from the logical argument to explaining scriptural reports.
Look for the phrase 'فكان تأويل ما ورد من الزيادة'.
2
Analyze the first interpretation
Understand the interpretation from Abu Hanifa and Ibn Abbas: believing in general (ijmal) then in detail (tafsir) does not increase the essence but adds specification.
Example: believing in all prophets generally vs. knowing each by name.
3
Examine the persistence interpretation
Consider the idea that persistence in iman every moment is like a continuous increase because each moment's affirmation is a new act, but this is not essential increase.
Nasafi uses the analogy of dirhams added one by one.
4
Distinguish light from essence
Learn that the third interpretation distinguishes between iman's essence and its light (nur), which can increase through righteous deeds and decrease through sins. Note the Quranic support.
This is the key resolution: scriptural talk of increase refers to light, not essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And since iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and it is in itself something that does not increase, and what does not increase has no decrease except by nonexistence, and no increase except by adding another like it to it. Thus there is no increase for iman by adding acts of obedience to it, nor decrease by committing sins, for tasdiq in both states remains as it was before. ?

?
If persistence in iman every moment is like adding a new dirham, do you actively renew your faith each day, or do you rely on a past affirmation? What is one 'obligation' from Allah you have not yet believed in detail?
?
The light of iman decreases with sins. Is there a sin you are holding onto that is dimming that light? What would it take for you to repent and restore that radiance, knowing your essence of iman remains intact?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
8 min
Faith Does Not Increase or Decrease in Its Essence
Al-Nasafi argues that iman as tasdiq does not increase or decrease and interprets scriptural evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Maturidi theology, the essence of faith (tasdiq) does not admit of increase or decrease, and how scriptural indications of increase are interpreted without contradicting this principle.

Core Idea
Faith as assent is indivisible; it cannot increase or decrease in its essence.

This passage from al-Nasafi lays out the Maturidi position that faith, defined as tasdiq (affirmation/assent), is a simple act of the heart that does not intrinsically increase or decrease. But how do we reconcile this with verses that speak of faith increasing? Al-Nasafi presents careful interpretations from Abu Hanifa and Ibn Abbas, distinguishing between summary belief and detailed specification, and between the essence of faith and its light in the heart. Let's work through his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of iman as tasdiq
Note that al-Nasafi begins by reaffirming that iman is al-tasdiq (affirmation/assent). This definition is crucial because it establishes that faith is a simple, indivisible act of the heart.
This definition is the foundation of all that follows.
2
Grasp the argument that what does not increase cannot decrease
Al-Nasafi argues that tasdiq, being something that does not undergo increase (in itself), can only decrease by total absence and only increase by addition of its like, which is impossible for a simple act.
This logical principle prohibits any quantitative change in the essence of faith.
3
Examine the interpretation of increase as tafsir over ijmal
To account for scriptural references to increase, al-Nasafi presents the interpretation from Abu Hanifa and Ibn Abbas: believers first believed in summary (ijmal), then as new commands came, they believed in detail (tafsir), resulting in an increase in articulation, not in the essence of tasdiq.
This reconciles the verses without compromising the definition of faith.
4
Consider persistence and steadfastness as a form of increase
Al-Nasafi adds that steadfastness in faith over time can be considered an increase analogously, like adding dirhams each hour, but this is not an increase in the essence itself, which is indivisible.
This further clarifies that any perceived increase is external to the core act of assent.
5
Distinguish between essence and its light
Finally, al-Nasafi allows that the light and brightness of faith in the heart can increase with good deeds and decrease with sins, citing Qur'anic verses. He concludes that the essence of tasdiq itself is not subject to change.
This handles the experiential aspect of faith while preserving theological consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص]: وإذا كان الإيمان هو التصديق وهو في نفسه مما لا يتزايد وما لا يتزايد فلا نقصان له إلا بالعدم ولا زيادة عليه إلا بانضمام مثله إليه، فلا زيادة إذا للإيمان بانضمام الطاعات إليه، ولا نقصان بارتكاب المعاصي، إذ التصديق في الحالين على ما كان قبلهما فكان تأويل ما ورد من الزيادة في الإيمان على ما روى عن أبي حنيفة - رحمه الله - أنهم كانوا آمنوا في الجملة ثم يأتي فرض بعد فرض فيؤمن بكل فرض جاء فيزداد إيمانه بالتفسير مع إيمانه بالجملة وإن كان بالجملة في التحقيق إيمان به، وقد روى عن ابن عباس - رضي الله عنهما - هذا التأويل أيضا وكذا الثبات على الإيمان والدوام عليه زيادة عليه في كل ساعة إذ يوجد في كل ساعة مثل ما انعدم في الأولى كما يوجد درهم ثم يزداد عليه في كل ساعة درهم إلا أن تلك الزيادة في نفسه إذ هو غير محتمل للتجزؤ، ويحتمل الزيادة عليه أن يزداد نوره وضياؤه في القلوب بالأعمال الصالحة وينتقص ذلك بالمعاصي إذ الإيمان له ضياء ونور على ما قال تعالى: ﴿ يُرِيدُونَ لِيُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْوَاهِهِمْ ﴾ وقال تعالى: ﴿ أَفَمَن شَرَحَ اللهُ صَدْرَهُ لِلإِسْلَامِ فَهُوَ عَلَى نُورٍ مِّن رَّبِّهِ ﴾ فأما هو في ذاته فلا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان على ما بينا.
[Faith does not increase or decrease]: And when faith (al-īmān) is affirmation/assent (al-taṣdīq), and it is in itself something that does not undergo increase, and what does not undergo increase has no decrease except by non-existence and no increase except by the addition of its like, then there is no increase for faith by the addition of acts of obedience to it, nor decrease by committing sins, since the affirmation/assent in both states is as it was before them. So the interpretation of what has been reported concerning increase in faith is according to what was narrated from Abū Ḥanīfa - may God have mercy on him - that they had believed in summary (al-jumla), then a command came after a command, so he believed in every command that came, so his faith increased by detailed specification (al-tafsīr) together with his faith in summary, although in reality the summary is faith in it. And it was narrated from Ibn ʿAbbās - may God be pleased with them both - this interpretation as well. Likewise, steadfastness upon faith and persistence in it is an increase over it every moment, since at every moment there exists the like of what was absent in the first, just as a dirham exists and then an increase of a dirham is added to it every moment, except that that increase is not in itself, for it is not susceptible to division. However, it is susceptible that its light and brightness in the hearts increase through righteous deeds and decrease through sins, since faith has illumination and light according to what the Exalted said: {They wish to extinguish the light of God with their mouths} and the Exalted said: {Then is he whose breast God has expanded for Islam, so he is upon a light from his Lord}. As for it in its essence, it does not admit of increase or decrease according to what we have explained.
Source pages p. 1093

Commentary
This passage is a definition and argument. Al-Nasafi begins by reiterating the Maturidi definition of iman as tasdiq (affirmation/assent). He then argues that tasdiq, being a simple act of the heart, does not intrinsically admit of increase or decrease; any increase would require the addition of another like of it, which is impossible for an indivisible unit. Consequently, acts of obedience do not increase iman, nor do sins decrease it. To reconcile scriptural references to increase (e.g., 'they increased in faith'), he presents the interpretation attributed to Abu Hanifa and Ibn Abbas: the increase is in tafsir (detailed specification) over ijmal (summary belief). For example, when a new obligation is revealed, the believer already believed in it summarily, but believing in it in detail constitutes an increase in the sense of fuller articulation, not in the essence of tasdiq. Additionally, persistence and steadfastness in iman over time can be seen as an increase analogously to adding dirhams every hour, but this is not an increase in the essence of iman itself. Al-Nasafi then allows for a qualitative increase: the light and brightness of iman in the heart can wax with good deeds and wane with sins, quoting verses about God's light. He concludes that the essential act of tasdiq itself is not subject to quantitative increase or decrease.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-īmān)
التصديق (al-taṣdīq)
الجملة (al-jumla)
التفسير (al-tafsīr)
الزيادة (al-ziyāda)
النقصان (al-nuqṣān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman increases with good deeds and decreases with sins in its very essence.
Correction: According to Maturidi theology, the essence of iman (tasdiq) does not increase or decrease; only its light and brightness can vary with deeds.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Nasafi, what is the core definition of faith (iman)?
A) Belief plus actions
B) Affirmation/assent (tasdiq)
C) Verbal confession
D) Knowledge of God

Key Takeaway
The essence of faith (tasdiq) is an indivisible act of the heart that does not increase or decrease; scriptural references to increase refer to detailed articulation or the light of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you felt your faith had decreased because of a sin you committed. According to this lesson, what actually changed? Does this realization free you from despair? Will you still strive to avoid sin even though it doesn't affect the essence of your iman? Why?
?
You hear the Quran and renew your shahada every day. In light of this lesson, does repeating the declaration increase your iman in its essence? If not, what is the purpose of repeating it? How does this lesson change the way you approach acts of worship—are you seeking an increase in essence or in the light of faith?
?
This lesson teaches that the essence of iman is a single, indivisible act of assent. Have you ever doubted whether you truly have that core assent? If so, how does this lesson reassure you or challenge you? What will you do today to strengthen the light of your faith, knowing the core is already secure?

Refuting Actions as Part of Faith
Al-Nasafi refutes those who include actions in faith with two logical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Nasafi argues that including actions in iman leads to logical contradictions, and how he distinguishes between increase in actions and increase in iman.

Core Idea
Including actions in faith makes faith impossible to complete and leads to absurdities.

Al-Nasafi now tackles a major theological dispute: whether actions are part of iman (faith) or are separate. He refutes the view that actions are constitutive of iman by exposing its logical flaws. This passage shows the devastating consequences of confusing acts of obedience with the inward assent that defines true faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of refutation
Al-Nasafi specifies which group is most entitled to avoid claiming increase in iman: those who include actions in its definition. Understand why he targets this group.
2
First argument: increase on incomplete is impossible
If all actions are iman, then iman is never complete because new acts arise. Increase on something incomplete is logically impossible. Trace this reasoning.
3
Second argument: increase on infinite is impossible
If iman includes all possible acts, it is infinite. Adding to an infinite whole is impossible. Al-Nasafi clarifies that increase must be upon a finite end.
4
Counter-response and Al-Nasafi's reply
The opponent might say iman is initially deficient and increases with each act. Al-Nasafi retorts that this would make the prophets' iman deficient. Follow this exchange.
5
Final distinction: iman vs. actions
Al-Nasafi reiterates that iman is only tasdiq (assent). Actions coincide in the name 'obedience' but not in the name 'faith'. Increase applies to actions, not iman itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أحق الناس أن يمتنع عن القول بالزيادة على الإيمان هم الذين يجعلون الأعمال من الإيمان، وذلك لأنهم إذا جعلوا الأعمال كلها إيمانًا فلا أحد إذا استكمل الإيمان، والزيادة على ما هو لم يكمل بعد وهو في حد النقصان محال، ولأنه ما من عبادة توجد إلا وهي من الإيمان ولا شيء وراء الكل ليتصور أن يكون زيادة باتصاله به. يوضحه أن الزيادة تكون على ذي النهاية فينتهى ثم يزاد عليه، فأما الزيادة على ما لا نهاية له فمحال إلا أن يقول الإيمان في حق الكل في حد النقصان ثم يزداد بكل طاعة، فمن كانت طاعاته أكثر كان إيمانه أكثر، فيقال له إذا على زعمك أن الإيمان غير متصور فكان إيمان كل نبي ومرسل ناقصاً، ثم نقول: إنا بينا أن الإيمان هو التصديق، وما وجد من الأعمال يساويه في اسم الطاعة والعبادة دون اسم الإيمان، فبوجود شيء منها يزداد من حيث المعنى الذي يشاركه في الاسم دون الذي يخالفه، فيكون بزيادة عمل يوجد ازدياد عباداته وطاعاته لا زيادة إيمانه.
Then the people most entitled to refrain from saying that there is increase in faith are those who make actions part of faith. That is because if they make all actions faith, then no one completes faith, and increase upon what has not yet been completed — while it is in a state of deficiency — is impossible. And because no act of worship exists except that it is from faith, and there is nothing beyond the whole for which an increase could be conceived by its conjunction. He clarifies it: increase is upon something finite, so it ends and then increase is added to it. As for increase upon what has no end, it is impossible. Unless one says that faith in relation to the whole is in a state of deficiency, then it increases with every act of obedience; so whoever has more acts of obedience has more faith. Then it is said to him: then according to your claim, since faith is not conceivable [as finite], the faith of every prophet and messenger would be deficient. Then we say: we have explained that faith is affirmation/assent (al-taṣdīq), and what exists of actions coincides with it in the name of obedience and worship, not in the name of faith. So by the existence of something from them, it increases from the perspective of the meaning that shares the name with it, not from the perspective that differs from it. Thus, by the increase of an act, there occurs an increase in his acts of worship and obedience, not an increase in his faith.
Source pages p. 1093

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. Al-Nasafi identifies the party that should most avoid claiming increase in iman: those who include actions (aʿmāl) in its definition. He presents two arguments against their position. First, if all actions are iman, then no one can ever complete iman, because new obligations arise continually. Increase on something incomplete is impossible because it implies a state of deficiency. Second, if iman is infinite (since it encompasses all possible acts of worship), adding something to an infinite whole is impossible. The opponent might respond by saying that iman is initially deficient and then increases with each act, so each person's iman is proportionate to his deeds. Al-Nasafi replies that this would entail that the prophets' iman is deficient, since they too could not have completed all possible acts. Finally, he reiterates his school's position: iman is only tasdiq (assent). Actions are not part of iman but share the name 'obedience' or 'worship'. When a person performs an act, his obedience increases, not his iman. Thus, increase in actions is misconstrued as increase in iman.

Key Terms
الأعمال (al-aʿmāl)
الطاعة (al-ṭāʿa)
العبادة (al-ʿibāda)
التصديق (al-taṣdīq)
الزيادة (al-ziyāda)
النقصان (al-nuqṣān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that including actions in iman supports the idea of increase in faith.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows this leads to contradictions: either iman is never complete or infinite, both making increase impossible. True increase is only in actions, not iman.

Checkpoint
What logical problem does Al-Nasafi identify for those who make actions part of iman?
A) They cannot explain how iman is a simple act
B) If all actions are iman, then no one can ever complete iman
C) They rely on weak hadith
D) They deny the light of iman

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi demonstrates that actions are not part of iman but are separate, and increase applies only to obedience, not to iman itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Why Including Actions in Faith Makes Increase Impossible
Imam al-Nasafi argues against faith including actions, using two logical proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the view that actions are part of faith leads to the impossibility of increase in faith.

Core Idea
If actions are faith, no one has complete faith, so increase is impossible.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful critique against those who consider actions to be part of faith. He argues that this position leads to logical absurdities, including the impossibility of anyone having complete faith and the impossibility of increase. This lesson walks through his two main arguments and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then read the English translation to get a full sense of the argument.
The passage is dense, so take your time.
2
Identify the first argument
The first argument: if all actions are faith, no one can have complete faith because there is always the potential for more actions. Increase on something that is not yet complete (i.e., still deficient) is impossible.
Notice the phrase 'لا أحد إذا استكمل الإيمان' (no one attains complete faith).
3
Identify the second argument
The second argument: increase is only possible on finite things. Since actions are potentially infinite, increase on an infinite set is absurd.
The author says 'الزيادة على ما لا نهاية له فمحال' (increase on what has no end is impossible).
4
Examine the counter-argument and refutation
The opponent might say faith is always in a state of deficiency and increases with each act. The author refutes this by pointing out that this would make even prophets have deficient faith.
This shows the unacceptable consequence of the opponent's position.
5
Reflect and apply
Consider how this argument reinforces the Maturidi position that faith is solely tasdiq (affirmation) and does not increase or decrease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان على ما بينا ، ثم أحق الناس أن يمتنع عن القول بالزيادة على الإيمان هم الذين يجعلون الأعمال من الإيمان، وذلك لأنهم إذا جعلوا الأعمال كلها إيمانًا فلا أحد إذا استكمل الإيمان، والزيادة على ما هو لم يكمل بعد وهو في حد النقصان ،محال، ولأنه ما من عبادة توجد إلا وهي من الإيمان ولا شيء وراء الكل ليتصور أن يكون زيادة باتصاله به. :يوضحه أن الزيادة تكون على ذي النهاية فينتهى ثم يزاد عليه، فأما الزيادة على ما لا نهاية له فمحال إلا أن يقول الإيمان في حق الكل في حد النقصان ثم يزداد بكل طاعة ، فمن كانت طاعاته أكثر كان إيمانه أكثر ، فيقال له إذا على زعمك كما الإيمان غير متصور فكان إيمان كل نبي ومرسل ناقصاً
It accepts increase and decrease according to what we clarified. Then the most entitled people to refrain from saying increase in faith are those who make actions part of faith. That is because if they make all actions faith, then no one attains complete faith, and increase on what is not yet complete and is in the state of deficiency is impossible. And because there is no act of worship that exists except that it is from faith, and there is nothing beyond the whole for an increase to be conceived by its connection to it. He clarifies it: Increase is on something finite; it ends and then something is added to it. As for increase on what has no end, it is impossible, unless one says that faith in the case of everyone is in the state of deficiency, then it increases with every act of obedience. So whoever has more acts of obedience has more faith. So it is said to him: then according to your claim, as faith is not conceivable, then the faith of every prophet and messenger would be deficient.
Source pages p. 1094

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that faith includes actions and therefore can increase. The author argues that if all actions are faith, then no one can ever have complete faith because there is always a possibility of more actions. Increase on something that is not yet complete (i.e., deficient) is impossible because it would require it to first be complete. Furthermore, there is no action outside the set of all actions to be added. He clarifies that increase applies only to finite things; trying to increase an infinite set is absurd. If the opponent claims that faith is in a state of deficiency for everyone and increases with each act, then even prophets would have deficient faith, which is untenable.

Key Terms
زيادة الإيمان
نقصان الإيمان
الأعمال من الإيمان
التصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that if actions are part of faith, then faith can increase through good deeds.
Correction: The author shows that this leads to the impossibility of complete faith and the absurdity of infinite increase, implying that faith must be solely tasdiq (affirmation) and does not increase.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Including actions in the definition of faith leads to logical absurdities, reinforcing that faith is simply affirmation (tasdiq) and does not increase or decrease.

The Analogy of Men and Women in a House
Imam al-Nasafi uses an analogy to show that actions increase acts of obedience, not faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Imam al-Nasafi, actions increase acts of obedience but not faith, using the analogy of men and women in a house.

Core Idea
Actions increase obedience, not faith, just as a woman increases persons, not men.

Imam al-Nasafi has already established that faith is only assent (tasdiq). Now he addresses an apparent implication: if actions are separate, do they increase faith? Responding with a clear analogy, he distinguishes between categories that share a name but differ in essence. This lesson unpacks that logical move.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: a logical claim followed by an analogy.
The analogy is central to the argument.
2
Identify the core claim
Find the sentence where al-Nasafi states that actions increase acts of worship and obedience, not faith. This is the point he is proving.
The key phrase is 'فيكون بزيادة عمل يوجد ازدياد عباداته وطاععاته لا زيادة إيمانه'.
3
Analyze the analogy
Break down the analogy: ten men in a house, a woman enters. She increases 'persons' and 'human beings' but not 'men'. Map each element to the theological claim: faith is like 'men', actions are like 'women', and the increase is in 'persons' (acts of obedience).
Consider the limits: the analogy is not about gender hierarchy but about genus and species.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: إنا بينا أن الإيمان هو التصديق، وما وجد من الأعمال يساويه في اسم الطاعة والعبادة دون اسم الإيمان، فبوجود شيء منها يزداد من حيث المعنى الذي يشاركه في الاسم دون الذي يخالفه، فيكون بزيادة عمل يوجد ازدياد عباداته وطاععاته لا زيادة إيمانه، كما إذا كان في بيت عشرة من الرجال فدخلت امرأة ذلك البيت كان دخولها يوجب زيادة في الأشخاص والآدميين دون الرجال حتى إن من قال ازداد بدخولها الأشخاص كان صادقًا، وإن قال ازداد الرجال كان كاذبًا فكذا هذا، والله الموفق.
Then we say: We have clarified that faith is assent (al-tasdiq), and that what exists of actions shares with it in the name of obedience and worship, not in the name of faith. So by the existence of something from them, one increases in terms of the meaning that shares the name, not in terms of the meaning that differs. So with the increase of an action, there is an increase in his acts of worship and acts of obedience, not an increase in his faith. Just as if there were ten men in a house, and a woman entered that house, her entry would cause an increase in persons and human beings but not in men, so that whoever says 'the persons increased by her entry' is truthful, and whoever says 'the men increased' is lying. So is this. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 1094

Commentary
This passage is an argument by analogy. The author restates his position that faith is only assent (tasdiq), while actions are a separate category that share the name 'obedience' but not 'faith'. When a person performs an action, his acts of obedience increase, but his faith does not increase because faith is not the kind of thing that increases by adding actions. The analogy: a house with ten men; a woman enters. The number of persons increases but not the number of men. Similarly, actions increase the count of obedient acts but not the essence of faith.

Key Terms
التصديق
الطاعة
العبادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The analogy implies that women are inferior or not part of faith.
Correction: The analogy is purely logical: it contrasts genus (persons) and species (men). The woman represents actions (a different category), not a judgment on gender. The point is about category membership, not value.

Checkpoint
What does the analogy of the ten men and the woman demonstrate?
A) Faith increases with actions.
B) Actions increase acts of obedience but not faith.
C) Women are not part of faith.
D) Men have more faith than women.

Key Takeaway
Actions increase acts of obedience, not faith itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that your actions do not increase your faith itself. If that is the case, what is truly motivating your daily worship? Are you seeking to deepen your inner conviction (tasdiq) or merely stacking up acts of obedience? Today, before your next prayer, pause and ask: is this prayer an act of faith from the heart or a habit of obedience? Commit to one moment of conscious tasdiq during your next act of worship.
?
The analogy shows that adding a woman to a house increases persons but not men. In your spiritual life, are you content with increasing the 'persons'—the outward acts—while the 'men'—your core faith—remains untouched? What would it take for your faith itself to grow? Identify one thing you can do today that directly targets your tasdiq, not just your to-do list of good deeds.
?
If faith does not increase with actions, then your salvation depends on the initial assent. Have you ever genuinely examined the strength of your tasdiq? Or have you relied on your deeds to feel secure? Imagine standing before Allah with your deeds weighed—what if your tasdiq is weak? Write down a single step you will take this week to reinforce your inner conviction, not just your outward compliance.

Refutation of Faith Decreasing by Sin
Imam al-Nasafi refutes faith decreasing by sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi uses a reductio argument to refute the claim that faith can decrease by sin.

Core Idea
Faith as assent cannot be partly lost; it either remains complete or becomes disbelief.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a striking logical refutation. The opponents hold that a new believer's faith can be diminished by a subsequent sin. Using their own premise—that faith is nothing but assent (tasdiq)—he shows this is impossible. The argument forces a contradiction: either faith remains intact or it vanishes into disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the astonishment expressed at the beginning.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and premise
The opponent claims that a believer's faith can decrease by sin. But what is faith according to them? It is only assent (tasdiq). Find where the author states this.
3
Trace the reductio argument
The author argues: if assent could be impaired, it would become its opposite (denial). If it is not impaired, it remains complete. So the claim of deficiency is contradictory. Map out these two branches.
This is the core logical move.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that the view of faith decreasing by sin is false. Ask yourself: does this argument depend on defining faith purely as assent?
This connects to broader debates about the nature of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العجب منهم أنهم يزعمون أن كافرًا لو أسلم وصدق بجميع ما يجب تصديقه صار مؤمنا ثم لو ارتكب من ساعته إثمًا انتقل إيمانه وليس معه إلا التصديق والتصديق لا تزايد له ولو اختل لتبدل بالتكذيب وبطل، ولو لم يختل بقى كاملاً فكان القول ببقائه وثبوت النقص فيه باطلاً.
Then it is astonishing from them that they claim that if a disbeliever were to accept Islam and affirm all that must be affirmed, he becomes a believer, then if he were to commit a sin immediately, his faith would transfer [or: decrease], while he has nothing but assent, and assent does not admit increase. If it were impaired, it would change into denial and become invalid, and if it were not impaired, it would remain complete, so the claim of its remaining and the establishment of deficiency in it is false.
Source pages p. 1095

Commentary
This passage presents a reductio ad absurdum. The opponents believe that faith can decrease by sin. But if faith is merely assent (tasdiq), it does not admit of partial loss. If it were damaged, it would become disbelief. So the idea that it can remain but be deficient is contradictory. Therefore, the claim that sin reduces faith is false.

Key Terms
التصديق
الزيادة
النقصان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A believer's faith can be partially lost or decreased by sinning while still remaining a believer.
Correction: If faith is defined as assent, it is an all-or-nothing state. It cannot be partially lost; either it is complete or it turns into disbelief. Thus, sin does not decrease faith but may lead to loss of faith entirely if it contradicts assent.

Checkpoint
What conclusion does the author draw from the opponent's claim that a believer's faith can decrease by sin?
A) That faith is not real.
B) That the opponent's view leads to contradiction.
C) That sin does not affect faith at all.
D) That the disbeliever's faith was incomplete.

Key Takeaway
The claim that faith can decrease by sin is self-contradictory because faith as assent is indivisible; it either remains complete or becomes disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have moments when, after a sin, you feel your faith has 'dipped.' But if faith is all-or-nothing assent, what is that feeling? Is it a timely warning from your soul or a delusion that leads you to underestimate the gravity of sin? Will you search your heart today to see if there is any belief you truly hold back from affirming?
?
Consider the scenario: a new Muslim sins moments after his shahada. According to this passage, his faith is either intact or gone. Do you think his faith is less than yours despite your years of obedience? If faith does not decrease, what excuse have you for neglecting your obligations? Will you recommit to action, knowing that your faith is whole but your deeds must reflect it?
?
The passage declares that the claim of faith remaining with deficiency is false. This means you cannot comfort yourself with 'I still believe, just a little less.' Either your heart fully affirms Allah and His Messenger or it does not. In the private corners of your life, where no one sees, is your assent truly complete? If there is any reservation, any doubt, any condition you place on your belief, will you confront it now and ask Allah for firmness?

Refuting the Claim that the Verse Shows Incomplete Faith
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the claim that the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' proves faith was incomplete before.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' does not imply that faith was incomplete before, and how this argument preserves the completeness of faith of the early Companions.

Core Idea
The perfection of religion in the Quran does not mean the faith of the early Muslims was deficient.

The verse about perfecting religion is sometimes used to argue that religion was incomplete before. This lesson examines Imam al-Nasafi's refutation of that claim, showing its absurd consequences regarding the status of the Prophet and his Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to understand the overall argument.
Notice that the passage is a refutation starting with 'That is false'.
2
Identify the opponents' claim
The opponents argue that the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' shows religion was deficient before. Find this claim in the passage.
3
Understand the reductio argument
The author uses a reductio ad absurdum: if the claim were true, then the earlier Companions and the Prophet himself would have been following a deficient religion. That is absurd.
This is a classic theological argument showing the logical outcome of the opponents' view.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the author mentions the specific sacrifices of the Emigrants and Helpers (Badr, pledges, hardships). This highlights the greatness of their faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: الْيَوْمَ أكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ أنه دليل أن الدين كان إلى ذلك اليوم ناقصا. باطل، لأن ذلك يوجب على قولهم أن من مات قبل ذلك من المهاجرين والأنصار الذين شهدوا بدرا وبايعوا رسول الله عليه السلام البيعتين جميعًا وبذلوا أنفسهم الله تعالى بمكة مع عظيم ما حل بهم من نكاية العدو وأنواع البلايا كلهم ماتوا على دين ناقص، وكذلك كان رسول الله عليه السلام يدعوهم إلى دين ناقص، وكان يوالي ويعادي عليه، وصاحب هذا القول على دين كامل فإذا سعى في مدح نفسه وتزكيتها وتقديمها على من يعلم أنه بجميع سعيه لا يبلغ مقامًا واحدًا من
And their attachment to His saying, exalted: 'Today I have perfected your religion' as evidence that the religion was deficient until that day is false. Because that would necessitate, according to their claim, that those who died before that from the Emigrants and the Helpers who witnessed Badr and gave the two pledges to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, altogether and sacrificed themselves for God in Mecca, despite the great affliction that befell them from the harm of the enemy and various trials, all of them died on a deficient religion. And likewise, the Messenger of God would have invited them to a deficient religion, and he would have allied and enmity upon it. And the holder of this claim is on a complete religion, so if he seeks to praise and purify himself and prefer himself over those whom he knows that with all his effort they would not reach one station...
Source pages p. 1095

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection based on Quran 5:3, 'Today I have perfected your religion.' The opponents argue that this shows the religion was previously incomplete, implying that faith (as part of religion) could increase. The author responds that if this were true, then all the earlier Muslims, including the Companions who made great sacrifices, died on an incomplete religion, and the Prophet himself would have been calling to an incomplete religion. This is clearly false, so the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
إكمال الدين
المهاجرين
الأنصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' means the religion (including faith) was incomplete and imperfect before its revelation.
Correction: The verse refers to the perfection of the legal and ritual aspects of the religion, not to the faith of individuals. The faith of the early Muslims, like the Companions, was complete at the time of their belief.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue would follow if the verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' implied prior deficiency?
A) That the earlier prophets had incomplete faith.
B) That the Companions who died before that died on a deficient religion.
C) That the religion was never complete.
D) That the verse is not from God.

Key Takeaway
The verse of perfection does not imply that the faith of earlier Muslims was deficient; rather, it affirms the completeness of the religion as a system.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear 'Today I have perfected your religion', do you ever subtly use it to feel that your own faith is more complete than that of the early Companions? What does that reveal about your heart?
?
The Companions endured unimaginable hardship—could you honestly say that your faith today has been tested to even a fraction of that degree? How would you measure your faith against theirs?
?
If you found yourself mocking or looking down on a Muslim whose practice differs from yours, would you be echoing the arrogance the author condemns? What step can you take today to honor those who sacrificed before you?

Faith Does Not Increase: The Analogy of Ten Men
The author uses an analogy to argue that faith does not increase or decrease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi school uses an analogy to argue that faith (iman) does not increase or decrease in its essence, remaining complete once affirmed.

Core Idea
Faith does not increase because its essence is affirmation, which cannot be more or less.

The author presents a simple analogy to illustrate a profound point: just as adding a woman to a group of men increases the number of persons but not the number of men, so too performing acts of obedience increases one's acts but not the essence of faith. This distinction is critical to understanding the Maturidi position that faith is verified by affirmation alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Get a feel for the author's argument before diving into analysis.
The passage has two parts: an analogy and its application to faith.
2
Understand the analogy
Focus on the analogy: ten men in a house, a woman enters. Why does the number of persons increase but not the number of men? Identify the key distinction between 'persons' (اشخاص) and 'men' (رجال).
The analogy shows that increase in a broader category does not imply increase in a specific subset.
3
Apply the analogy to faith
Now see how the author applies this: acts of obedience are like the woman's entry—they increase the general category of good deeds, but faith (the essence) does not increase because it is like 'men', a specific category (affirmation).
This is the core of the argument: affirmation (tasdiq) is the essence, and it is not quantifiable.
4
Consider the objection about sin
The author then addresses a potential objection: if a believer commits a sin, does faith decrease? He argues that since faith is only affirmation, and affirmation is either present (complete) or absent, sin cannot reduce it.
This refutes the idea of faith increasing or decreasing with deeds.
5
Summarize the key takeaway
Write a one-sentence summary of the argument: Faith is complete at the moment of sincere affirmation; subsequent sins do not diminish it, just as a woman entering a house does not increase the number of men.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا كان في بيت عشرة من الرجال فدخلت (۱) امرأة (۲) ذلك البيت (۳) كان دخولها يوجب زيادة في الأشخاص والآدميين (٤) دون الرجال حتى إن من قال ازداد بدخولها الأشخاص كان صادقًا، وإن قال ازداد () الرجال كان كاذبًا فكذا هذا، والله الموفق. ثم العجب منهم أنهم يزعمون أن كافرًا لو أسلم وصدق بجميع ما يجب تصديقه صار مؤمنا ثم لو ارتكب من ساعته إثمًا انتقل إيمانه وليس معه إلا التصديق والتصديق (٦) لا تزايد له ولو اختل لتبدل بالتكذيب وبطل، ولو لم يختل بقى كاملاً فكان القول ببقائه وثبوت النقص فيه باطلاً.
If there are ten men in a house, and a woman enters that house, her entry necessitates an increase in persons and human beings but not in men, such that if one says 'the persons have increased by her entry' he is truthful, and if he says 'the men have increased' he is false. So likewise this. And Allah is the Granter of success. Then the wonder is from them that they claim that if a disbeliever becomes Muslim and affirms all that must be affirmed, he becomes a believer, then if he commits a sin from his very hour, his faith transfers, and he has only affirmation, and affirmation does not admit increase; if it were to become defective, it would change by denial and become null, and if it does not become defective, it remains complete. So the statement of its remaining and the establishment of deficiency in it is false.
Source pages p. 1095

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that faith can increase or decrease. The author first presents an analogy: if a woman enters a house with ten men, the number of persons increases but the number of men does not. Similarly, faith (iman) is essentially affirmation (tasdiq); affirmation does not admit of increase in its essence. The author then applies this: if a disbeliever becomes a Muslim through affirmation, his faith is complete. If he subsequently commits a sin, his faith does not decrease because it would require a change in the affirmation itself, which would either nullify it if defective or leave it complete. Therefore, any claim of deficiency in faith is false.

Key Terms
الرجال
الأشخاص
الآدميين
التصديق
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that increase in acts of faith implies increase in the essence of faith.
Correction: The essence of faith is affirmation (tasdiq), which is indivisible; acts are separate and do not affect its quantity.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to argue that faith does not increase?
A) A house with ten men and a woman entering increases persons but not men.
B) A garden with trees that grow taller over time.
C) A ship with sailors where the crew size changes.
D) A river that floods its banks.

Key Takeaway
Faith, being affirmation, does not increase or decrease; it is complete the moment it is sincerely held.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith is complete affirmation that cannot be increased, then why do you sometimes feel your faith is 'weak'? Is it possible that what you call 'weak faith' is actually a failure to fully affirm? What would it take for you to stop measuring your faith by your feelings and instead rest on the certainty that your affirmation—if sincere—is already complete?
?
The author says that if affirmation becomes defective, it changes into denial. Are there areas in your life where you have allowed doubt or compromise to make your faith 'defective'—not because you deny, but because you treat certain commands as optional? How will you confront that one area today and reaffirm your complete trust?
?
Imagine you commit a major sin. According to this lesson, your faith does not decrease. Does that comfort you or trouble you? Are you tempted to use this as an excuse to sin, or does it drive you to a deeper gratitude that your faith is secure in Allah's grace, not your actions? What will you actually do the next time you sin to keep your affirmation pure?

Faith as Affirmation: A Real Inner Quality
Definition of faith as affirmation (tasdiq) with analogy to physical attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith (iman) is defined as genuine inner affirmation (tasdiq) of the Prophet's message, a real attribute that makes one a believer.

Core Idea
Faith is a real inner affirmation, not just a label.

The author opens a section on the final outcome by defining the very essence of faith. He insists that faith is not a mere legal status or verbal confession, but a true inner reality—affirmation (tasdiq) of everything the Prophet brought. This lesson unpacks that definition and its implications, drawing on the analogy with physical attributes like sitting and standing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation carefully. Notice the structure: the author first states that faith is a name for affirmation, then specifies its object and its reality, then draws an analogy.
The passage is incomplete; focus on what is present.
2
Understand the core definition
Faith = affirmation of Muhammad (peace be upon him) in what he brought from Allah. This is the central claim. Reflect on why the author calls it a 'real thing with a known definition'.
The author is countering views that see faith as merely external.
3
Examine the analogy
The author compares faith to physical attributes like sitting, standing, blackness, whiteness. Just as these are real qualities that describe a person, faith is a real internal quality that makes one a believer.
This analogy emphasizes that faith is an attribute of the essence (dhat).
4
Consider the incomplete ending
The passage cuts off mid-sentence. Based on context, the author likely continued to elaborate on how faith is a real meaning in the soul. Reflect on what might come next.
This shows the importance of studying the full text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة العاقبة
ثم الإيمان لما كان اسمًا للتصديق وهو على التلخيص تصديق محمد بما جاء به من عند الله تعالى وهو شيء حقيقي معلوم الحد، فإذا حصل بهذا الحد كان الذات به مؤمنا كالقعود والجلوس والسواد والبياض وغير ذلك لما كانت معاني
The Issue of the Consequence (or final outcome)
Then, since faith (al-iman) is a name for affirmation (al-tasdiq), and it is, according to the summary, the affirmation of Muhammad ﷺ in what he brought from Allah Almighty, and it is a real thing of known definition (hadd). So when it occurs with this definition, the essence (al-dhat) becomes a believer by it, like sitting, standing, blackness, whiteness, and other things, since they are meanings...
Source pages p. 1097

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a section titled 'The Issue of the Consequence' (مسألة العاقبة). The author defines faith (الإيمان) as affirmation (التصديق) – specifically, affirming Muhammad ﷺ in everything he brought from Allah. He emphasizes that this affirmation is a real thing (شيء حقيقي) with a known definition (معلوم الحد). When this quality occurs in a person according to that definition, the person's essence (الذات) is truly described as a believer, just as physical attributes like sitting, standing, blackness, or whiteness make the essence characterized by them. The author is establishing that faith is a real, inherent quality, not a mere label. The passage cuts off mid-sentence ('since they are meanings...'), likely continuing with further explanation.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think iman is merely verbal confession or a legal status without inner reality.
Correction: The passage defines iman as a real inner affirmation (tasdiq) that changes the essence of a person, analogous to physical attributes.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is faith (al-iman)?
A) A name for ritual prayer and charity.
B) A name for affirmation (tasdiq) of Muhammad's message, a real thing with a known definition.
C) Merely a legal status that does not affect the essence.
D) The same as Islam in all respects.

Key Takeaway
Faith is a real, inner affirmation of the Prophet's message, not a mere external label.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage compares faith to physical attributes like sitting or standing. Are you truly 'standing' in your faith with firm conviction, or are you merely resting in comfort, unaffected? Write down one area where your belief does not translate into action, and commit to a specific change by the end of this week.
?
Faith here is called a 'real thing with a known definition.' Do you know what your faith actually means, or have you simply adopted a vague belief? Take five minutes to write your own definition of iman based on this passage, and then ask yourself if you live by that definition.
