Faith and Disbelief
beginner
4 min
The Reality of Faith as Affirmation
Al-Nasafi defines faith as affirmation and analogizes it to other real attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith (iman) is a real attribute of inner affirmation, analogous to physical attributes like sitting or blackness, and is defined by its present existence.

Core Idea
Faith is a real present attribute, not a future contingency.

Al-Nasafi begins by establishing the nature of faith as a real and definable reality. Before addressing the controversial doctrine of final outcome, he grounds the discussion in a clear definition: faith is affirmation (tasdiq) of the Prophet's message. This definition anchors the entire refutation that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of faith
Read the Arabic sentence defining faith as tasdiq. Notice that al-Nasafi calls it a 'real thing with a known limit' (shay' haqiqi ma'lum al-hadd).
The definition is concise: it is affirmation of Muhammad regarding what he brought from Allah.
2
Understand the analogy
Faith is compared to attributes like sitting, standing, blackness, and whiteness. Just as these are real when present, faith is real when affirmation occurs.
The analogy shows that faith is not merely a label but a concrete reality.
3
Connect to the main point
If faith is a real attribute, its presence or absence must be judged by the current state, not by future possibilities.
This sets up the refutation of the final-outcome doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الإيمان لما كان اسمًا للتصديق وهو على التلخيص تصديق محمد بما جاء به من عند الله تعالى وهو شيء حقيقي معلوم الحد، فإذا حصل بهذا الحد كان الذات به مؤمنا كالقعود والجلوس والسواد والبياض وغير ذلك لما كانت معاني معلومة الحد متى وجدت بحقيقتها كان الذات بها قاعدًا جالسًا أسود أبيض فكذا هذا، ثم إذا كان كذلك لا معنى لقول الأشعرية ومن تقدمهم من الخوارج كنجدة الحروري وطوائف من الناس أن لا عبرة لإيمان من وجد منه التصديق للحال ولا لكفر من وجد منه التكذيب بل العبرة للعاقبة، فإن كان في علم الله تعالى أن هذا الشخص المعين يختم له بالإيمان فهو للحال مؤمن وإن كان مكذبا لله تعالى ولرسوله عليه السلام ساجدًا للصنم، وإن كان في علمه أنه يختم له بالكفر – نعوذ بالله - يكون في الحال كافرًا وإن كان مصدقًا لله تعالى ولرسوله فهذا لا معنى له، لأن الحقائق لم تعرف معدومة باعتبار العلم أنها تنعدم فإن الله يعلم الحي حيا ولا يعلمه للحال ميتا وإن كان يعلم أنه يموت لا محالة، وكذا هذا من الجالس والقائم والأسود والأبيض وكل وصف وحال للآدمي، ولو كان الأمر على ما تزعمون لكان ينبغي أن نكون نحن الآن في الآخرة وأن كل ميت كان حيًا لأن عاقبة الأمر هكذا، وحيث كان هذا باطلاً خارجاً عن المعارف دل على بطلان ذلك المذهب، والله الموفق. فإن قالوا: أليس إذا علم الله تعالى أنه يختم له بالإيمان فهو ولي الله، وإذا علم أنه يختم له بالكفر فهو عدو الله تعالى؟ قلنا : الولاية والعداوة تكونان بالإيمان والكفر فمن كفر بعد إيمانه كان وليًا فصار عدواً وكذا القلب، والتغير على الولي والعدو دون الولاية والعداوة كما في العلم والمعلوم والإخبار والمخبر عنه، والله الموفق.
Then since faith is a name for affirmation, and in summary it is affirmation of Muhammad regarding what he brought from Allah, exalted, and it is a real thing with a known definition – so when it occurs according to this definition, the essence is thereby a believer, like sitting, standing, blackness, whiteness, and other things, since they are meanings with known definitions: whenever they occur in their reality, the essence is thereby sitting, standing, black, white. So likewise is this. Then if this is the case, there is no meaning to the statement of the Ash'arites and those before them from the Kharijites, like Najda al-Haruri, and groups of people, that there is no consideration for the faith of one from whom affirmation occurs presently, nor for the unbelief of one from whom denial occurs; rather consideration is for the final outcome. For if it is in the knowledge of Allah, exalted, that this particular person will be sealed with faith, then he is presently a believer, even if he is denying Allah and His Messenger, peace be upon him, and prostrating to an idol; and if it is in His knowledge that he will be sealed with unbelief – we seek refuge in Allah – he is presently an unbeliever, even if he affirms Allah and His Messenger. This has no meaning, because realities are not known as nonexistent due to the knowledge that they will cease to exist. For Allah knows the living as living and does not know him presently as dead, even though He knows that he will die without doubt. And likewise this applies to the sitting, the standing, the black, the white, and every description and state of the human. And if the matter were as you claim, it would follow that we are now in the Hereafter and that every dead person was alive, because the final outcome of the matter is thus. And since this is false and outside of known principles, it indicates the falsehood of that doctrine. And Allah is the granter of success. And if they say: 'Is it not the case that if Allah knows that he will be sealed with faith, then he is a friend of Allah, and if He knows that he will be sealed with unbelief, then he is an enemy of Allah?' We say: Friendship and enmity are by virtue of faith and unbelief. So whoever disbelieves after his faith was a friend and became an enemy, and likewise the reverse. And change applies to the friend and enemy, not to friendship and enmity, just as in knowledge and the known, and informing and the informed about. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 1097

Commentary
This passage refutes the doctrine of al-‘Aqiba (final outcome) held by Ash‘aris and earlier Kharijites. The author first defines faith (iman) as affirmation (tasdiq) of Prophet Muhammad concerning what he brought from God. Faith is a real attribute with a defined limit. When affirmation exists, the person is truly a believer in the present, just as sitting, standing, blackness, and whiteness are real attributes that define a subject when present. The Ash‘ari and Kharijite view is then presented: they claim that present faith or unbelief has no bearing; rather, only the final outcome (al-‘aqiba) matters according to God's foreknowledge. If God knows a person will die a believer, that person is presently a believer even if currently denying God and worshipping an idol. Conversely, if God knows a person will die an unbeliever, that person is presently an unbeliever even if currently affirming God. The author rejects this as meaningless, using the analogy of life and death: God knows the living as living, not as dead presently, though He knows they will die. Similarly, present attributes like sitting, standing, black, white are real now regardless of future change. If the logic of the opponent were valid, it would absurdly imply we are now in the Hereafter and every dead person is alive, since the final outcome of the world is resurrection. Since this is obviously false, the doctrine is false. An objection is then raised: if God knows one's final state, doesn't that make one a friend or enemy of God now? The author responds that friendship (wilaya) and enmity ('adawa) are based on present faith and unbelief. A person changes from friend to enemy by actually committing unbelief. Change applies to the person, not to the relationship itself, just as knowledge and information do not change the known object but reflect its state. Thus, God's knowledge does not alter the present reality of faith or unbelief.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does al-Nasafi describe faith in this passage?
A) As a future contingency determined by God's knowledge
B) As a real attribute with a known definition
C) As an outward action only
D) As an ambiguous concept

Key Takeaway
Faith is a present reality defined by inner affirmation, not a future outcome.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith is a real attribute like sitting or blackness, can you be 'partially sitting'? Then is it possible to be 'partially a believer'? What does that mean for the state of your heart right now, not tomorrow?
?
The analogy compares faith to physical properties that are outwardly observable. But your faith is hidden. If someone could see your heart as clearly as they see your skin color, would they see the 'blackness' of affirmation or the 'whiteness' of denial? Are you willing to have your inner reality exposed?
?
You will one day stand before Allah with only your affirmed belief in that moment. If your deathbed denial could wipe out a lifetime of affirmations, then faith would be a gamble. But this lesson says it is a present reality. So what are you doing today to ensure your affirmation is real, not just a future wish?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Refuting the Doctrine of Final Outcome
Al-Nasafi refutes the al-‘Aqiba doctrine using analogy and reduction to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari and Kharijite claim that final outcome determines present faith is invalid, using the analogy of life and death and reduction to absurdity.

Core Idea
Present realities are not negated by future knowledge.

Having established faith as a real attribute, al-Nasafi now directly refutes the doctrine of al-‘Aqiba. He argues that it is absurd to judge present faith by God's knowledge of the future, just as it is absurd to call a living person dead because God knows he will die.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's view
Identify the claim that present faith or unbelief is irrelevant; only the final outcome matters according to divine knowledge.
The Ash'aris and Kharijites like Najda al-Haruri held this view.
2
Study the analogy
The author uses the example of God knowing a living person as living, not as dead. Explain how this analogy refutes the opponent.
If God knows a person as dead only when they are dead, similarly He knows a person as a believer only when they actually affirm.
3
Consider the absurd consequence
If the opponent's logic were sound, it would imply we are now in the Hereafter and every dead person is alive. See why this is false.
This reduction to absurdity seals the refutation.
4
Conclude
The false consequence shows the doctrine is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الإيمان لما كان اسمًا للتصديق وهو على التلخيص تصديق محمد بما جاء به من عند الله تعالى وهو شيء حقيقي معلوم الحد، فإذا حصل بهذا الحد كان الذات به مؤمنا كالقعود والجلوس والسواد والبياض وغير ذلك لما كانت معاني معلومة الحد متى وجدت بحقيقتها كان الذات بها قاعدًا جالسًا أسود أبيض فكذا هذا، ثم إذا كان كذلك لا معنى لقول الأشعرية ومن تقدمهم من الخوارج كنجدة الحروري وطوائف من الناس أن لا عبرة لإيمان من وجد منه التصديق للحال ولا لكفر من وجد منه التكذيب بل العبرة للعاقبة، فإن كان في علم الله تعالى أن هذا الشخص المعين يختم له بالإيمان فهو للحال مؤمن وإن كان مكذبا لله تعالى ولرسوله عليه السلام ساجدًا للصنم، وإن كان في علمه أنه يختم له بالكفر – نعوذ بالله - يكون في الحال كافرًا وإن كان مصدقًا لله تعالى ولرسوله فهذا لا معنى له، لأن الحقائق لم تعرف معدومة باعتبار العلم أنها تنعدم فإن الله يعلم الحي حيا ولا يعلمه للحال ميتا وإن كان يعلم أنه يموت لا محالة، وكذا هذا من الجالس والقائم والأسود والأبيض وكل وصف وحال للآدمي، ولو كان الأمر على ما تزعمون لكان ينبغي أن نكون نحن الآن في الآخرة وأن كل ميت كان حيًا لأن عاقبة الأمر هكذا، وحيث كان هذا باطلاً خارجاً عن المعارف دل على بطلان ذلك المذهب، والله الموفق. فإن قالوا: أليس إذا علم الله تعالى أنه يختم له بالإيمان فهو ولي الله، وإذا علم أنه يختم له بالكفر فهو عدو الله تعالى؟ قلنا : الولاية والعداوة تكونان بالإيمان والكفر فمن كفر بعد إيمانه كان وليًا فصار عدواً وكذا القلب، والتغير على الولي والعدو دون الولاية والعداوة كما في العلم والمعلوم والإخبار والمخبر عنه، والله الموفق.
Then since faith is a name for affirmation, and in summary it is affirmation of Muhammad regarding what he brought from Allah, exalted, and it is a real thing with a known definition – so when it occurs according to this definition, the essence is thereby a believer, like sitting, standing, blackness, whiteness, and other things, since they are meanings with known definitions: whenever they occur in their reality, the essence is thereby sitting, standing, black, white. So likewise is this. Then if this is the case, there is no meaning to the statement of the Ash'arites and those before them from the Kharijites, like Najda al-Haruri, and groups of people, that there is no consideration for the faith of one from whom affirmation occurs presently, nor for the unbelief of one from whom denial occurs; rather consideration is for the final outcome. For if it is in the knowledge of Allah, exalted, that this particular person will be sealed with faith, then he is presently a believer, even if he is denying Allah and His Messenger, peace be upon him, and prostrating to an idol; and if it is in His knowledge that he will be sealed with unbelief – we seek refuge in Allah – he is presently an unbeliever, even if he affirms Allah and His Messenger. This has no meaning, because realities are not known as nonexistent due to the knowledge that they will cease to exist. For Allah knows the living as living and does not know him presently as dead, even though He knows that he will die without doubt. And likewise this applies to the sitting, the standing, the black, the white, and every description and state of the human. And if the matter were as you claim, it would follow that we are now in the Hereafter and that every dead person was alive, because the final outcome of the matter is thus. And since this is false and outside of known principles, it indicates the falsehood of that doctrine. And Allah is the granter of success. And if they say: 'Is it not the case that if Allah knows that he will be sealed with faith, then he is a friend of Allah, and if He knows that he will be sealed with unbelief, then he is an enemy of Allah?' We say: Friendship and enmity are by virtue of faith and unbelief. So whoever disbelieves after his faith was a friend and became an enemy, and likewise the reverse. And change applies to the friend and enemy, not to friendship and enmity, just as in knowledge and the known, and informing and the informed about. And Allah is the granter of success.

Answering the Objection on Divine Friendship and Enmity
Al-Nasafi responds to a potential objection regarding divine friendship and enmity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi responds to the objection that God's knowledge of final outcome implies present divine friendship or enmity, by distinguishing between the person and the relationship.

Core Idea
Friendship and enmity are based on actual faith and unbelief, not on foreknowledge.

After the main refutation, an objection is raised: if God knows a person's end, doesn't that make them a friend or enemy now? Al-Nasafi replies that friendship (wilaya) and enmity ('adawa) are attributes that follow actual faith and unbelief, not God's prior knowledge. A person who disbelieves after being a believer changes from friend to enemy, and vice versa.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The opponents argue that God's knowledge of final outcome must entail present friendship or enmity.
They ask: if God knows he will be sealed with faith, is he not a friend of Allah now?
2
Understand the response
Al-Nasafi distinguishes between the attributes (wilaya and 'adawa) and the persons (wali and 'adu). The attributes are based on the current state of faith, not on future knowledge.
He says: 'Friendship and enmity are by virtue of faith and unbelief.'
3
Reflect on the analogy
He compares it to knowledge and the known; knowledge does not change the known object but reflects its state.
Change applies to the person who believes or disbelieves, not to the abstract relationship.

Source Text

Refutation of the Muwafat View on Faith
Nasafi refutes the muwafat view on faith using logical analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Nasafi argues that present faith or disbelief is determined by actual tasdiq or takdhib, not by God's knowledge of the final outcome.

Core Idea
Present reality, not future knowledge, defines faith.

Imam Nasafi confronts a problematic view that ties a person's current faith to their final destiny. He argues that if someone affirms (tasdiq) now, they are a believer now, regardless of what God knows about their end. This short but powerful passage uses logical analogy and reductio ad absurdum to dismantle the muwafat (final outcome) position, and then answers a key objection about wilaya and 'adawa.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once and then its English translation. Get a feel for the flow of the argument before diving into analysis.
2
Identify the opening principle
Notice how Nasafi starts with a general rule about known realities: when something exists in its reality, the essence is described by that reality. This sets up the analogy for faith and disbelief.
This principle is key to understanding his refutation.
3
Understand the Ash'ari/Kharijite claim
Nasafi states the opposing view: that only the final outcome matters, not current acts. Find this claim and see how he calls it meaningless.
4
Follow the analogy and reductio
Nasafi uses the example of God knowing the living as living, not as dead, even though He knows they will die. Then he applies a reductio: if the opposing view were true, we would be in the afterlife now. Reflect on why this is absurd.
5
Examine the objection and answer
Read the objection about wilaya (friendship) and 'adawa (enmity) based on God's knowledge. Then see Nasafi's response: these relations depend on actual faith and disbelief, and change occurs on the person, not the relation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معلومة الحد متى وجدت بحقيقتها كان الذات بها قاعدًا جالسًا أسود أبيض فكذا هذا، ثم إذا كان كذلك لا معنى لقول الأشعرية ومن تقدمهم من الخوارج كنجدة الحروري وطوائف من الناس أن لا عبرة لإيمان من وجد منه التصديق للحال ولا لكفر من وجد منه التكذيب بل العبرة للعاقبة، فإن كان في علم الله تعالى أن هذا الشخص المعين يختم له بالإيمان فهو للحال مؤمن وإن كان مكذبا لله تعالى ولرسوله عليه السلام ساجدًا للصنم، وإن كان في علمه أنه يختم له بالكفر – نعوذ بالله - يكون في الحال كافرًا وإن كان مصدقًا لله تعالى ولرسوله فهذا لا معنى له، لأن الحقائق لم تعرف معدومة باعتبار العلم أنها تنعدم فإن الله يعلم الحي حيا ولا يعلمه للحال ميتا وإن كان يعلم أنه يموت لا محالة، وكذا هذا من الجالس والقائم والأسود والأبيض وكل وصف وحال للآدمي، ولو كان الأمر على ما تزعمون لكان ينبغي أن نكون نحن الآن في الآخرة وأن كل ميت كان حيًا لأن عاقبة الأمر هكذا، وحيث كان هذا باطلاً خارجاً عن المعارف دل على بطلان ذلك المذهب، والله الموفق. فإن قالوا: أليس إذا علم الله تعالى أنه يختم له بالإيمان فهو ولي الله، وإذا علم أنه يختم له بالكفر فهو عدو الله تعالى؟ قلنا : الولاية والعداوة تكونان بالإيمان والكفر فمن كفر بعد إيمانه كان وليًا فصار عدواً وكذا القلب، والتغير على الولي والعدو دون الولاية والعداوة كما في العلم والمعلوم والإخبار والمخبر عنه، والله الموفق.
The known actuality—whenever it exists in its reality — the essence is thereby sitting, standing, black, white; likewise this. Then, if it is so, there is no meaning to the statement of the Ash'aris and those before them among the Kharijites like Najda al-Haruri and groups of people that there is no consideration for the faith of one from whom tasdiq is found in the present state, nor for the disbelief of one from whom takdhib is found; rather the consideration is for the final outcome. For if it is in the knowledge of God Almighty that this specific person will be sealed with faith, then he is in the present state a believer even if he is denying God and His Messenger, prostrating to an idol; and if it is in His knowledge that he will be sealed with disbelief—may God protect us—then he is in the present state a disbeliever even if he is affirming God and His Messenger. This has no meaning, because realities are not known to be non-existent by virtue of knowledge that they will become non-existent. For God knows the living as living, and does not know him in the present state as dead, even though He knows that he will inevitably die. Likewise this applies to the sitting, standing, black, white, and every attribute and state of a human. And if the matter were as you claim, then it would be necessary that we be now in the afterlife, and that every dead person was alive, because the final outcome is thus. Since this is false and outside of knowledge, it proves the falsehood of that doctrine. And God is the Grantor of success. If they say: Does not God Almighty, when He knows that he will be sealed with faith, then he is a friend of God, and when He knows that he will be sealed with disbelief, then he is an enemy of God? We say: Friendship and enmity arise from faith and disbelief. So whoever disbelieves after his faith was a friend then becomes an enemy; and likewise the reverse. Change occurs upon the friend and enemy, not upon friendship and enmity, just as in knowledge and the known, and in informing and the informed about. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1098

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Ash'ari and Kharijite position that the final destiny (al-'aqiba) determines one's current status of faith (iman) or disbelief (kufr). The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by establishing a principle: when a known reality (mā'lūma al-ḥadd) actually exists with its true reality, the essence is described by that reality (e.g., sitting, standing, black, white). Then he applies this to faith and disbelief: tasdiq (affirmation) is the reality of iman, and takdhib (denial) is the reality of kufr. If these are present in a person now, then that person is truly a believer or disbeliever now, regardless of future knowledge. The Ash'ari claim that only the final state matters leads to absurdities: it would mean that if God knows someone will die a believer, that person is currently a believer even if he is actually denying God and prostrating to idols; conversely, if God knows he will die a disbeliever, he is currently a disbeliever even if he affirms God. Nasafi calls this meaningless because realities are not negated by future knowledge. He gives an analogy: God knows a living person as living, and does not know him as dead now even though He knows he will die. Similarly, all attributes (sitting, standing, etc.) are judged by present actuality, not future expectation. If the Ash'ari view were correct, we would have to consider ourselves now in the afterlife (since we will all die) and every dead person as alive now—which is clearly false. Thus the doctrine is invalid. Then he addresses an objection: If God knows someone will be a believer in the end, doesn't that make him a friend (wali) of God now? Nasafi replies that friendship (wilaya) and enmity ('adawa) are based on actual faith and disbelief. A person who disbelieves after having faith was a friend but becomes an enemy; the reverse also holds. Change occurs on the person (the friend/enemy), not on the relationship of friendship/enmity itself, just as knowledge and the known change but the relation remains. Thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
التكذيب
العاقبة
الولاية
العداوة
علم الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's foreknowledge of a person's final state makes their current actions irrelevant to their faith status.
Correction: Nasafi argues that present faith is defined by actual tasdiq or takdhib, not by future knowledge. God knows the living as living now, not as dead, even though He knows they will die.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Nasafi use to refute the claim that final destiny determines current faith?
A) God knows the living as living, not as dead now
B) God knows all things equally
C) The afterlife is present now
D) Faith is only known by God

Key Takeaway
Present faith is defined by actual tasdiq or takdhib, not by God's knowledge of the final outcome.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you postpone sincere repentance, relying on God's mercy to cover your current disobedience while hoping for a good end? This passage says your present reality defines your status. What is your present reality before God right now—tasdiq or takdhib? What will you change today to align with it?
?
The Ash'ari view allowed people to feel safe in sin if they assumed God's foreknowledge would save them. Are you using God's unseen mercy as a license to delay obedience? How does this lesson strip away that excuse? Answer with one concrete step you will take before today ends.
?
Nasafi says God knows the living as living, not as dead. If God saw you in this moment, what would He see? Not what you plan to be tomorrow, but what you are right now. Are you truly affirming Him with your heart and actions, or are you living in a contradiction? Write down one area where your present belief does not match your practice—and commit to changing it this week.

The Identity of Iman and Islam
Nasafi states that iman and islam are one and the same thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Imam al-Nasafi (Maturidi), iman and islam are the same thing, with no distinction between them.

Core Idea
Iman and Islam are synonymous terms for the same reality.

In this short passage, Imam al-Nasafi builds on the previous definition of iman as tasdiq (heartfelt assent) to make a bold claim: iman and islam are one and the same. He asserts that the terms are synonymous and that every believer is a muslim and every muslim is a believer. This sets the Maturidi position apart from those who differentiate between the two concepts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the logical flow: 'when it is known that iman is tasdiq, we know that iman and islam are one thing...'
The passage cuts off after 'because', but the main claim is complete.
2
Understand the key premise
The author starts from the premise that iman is tasdiq (assent). This is the foundation for claiming identity with islam.
3
Grasp the conclusion of identity
From that premise, Nasafi concludes that iman and islam are the same thing (شيء واحد) and their names are synonymous (مترادفة). This means the two terms refer to the same reality.
4
Reflect on the implication
If they are synonymous, then every mu'min is a muslim and every muslim is a mu'min. This directly opposes views that separate iman from islam.
This is a key Maturidi doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرف أن الإيمان هو التصديق عرفنا أن الإيمان والإسلام شيء واحد، والأسماء من قبيل الأسماء المترادفة، وكل مؤمن مسلم وكل مسلم مؤمن، وذلك لأن
And when it is known that iman is tasdiq (assent), we know that iman and islam are one thing, and the names are among synonymous names, and every believer (mu'min) is a muslim and every muslim is a believer. And that is because...
Source pages p. 1100

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi position that iman and islam are identical. The author begins with the established premise that iman is tasdiq (assent of the heart). From this, he concludes that iman and islam are one entity, and the terms are synonymous. This means that every mu'min (believer) is a muslim and every muslim is a mu'min. The argument is cut off at 'because', but the reasoning likely proceeds to explain that since islam is submission to Allah, and that submission is the same as the assent of the heart, they are equivalent. This refutes those who separate iman and islam into distinct categories.

Key Terms

إسلام (submission)
تصديق (assent)
مترادفة (synonymous)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some hold that iman and islam are distinct, e.g., iman is only in the heart while islam includes outward acts.
Correction: Nasafi asserts they are identical and synonymous; every mu'min is a muslim and vice versa, based on the definition of iman as tasdiq.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the relationship between iman and islam?
A) Iman is part of islam.
B) Islam is part of iman.
C) They are the same thing.
D) They are unrelated.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Nasafi affirms that iman and islam are identical, both referring to the inner assent (tasdiq), making the terms synonymous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Nasafi says every believer is a Muslim and every Muslim is a believer. Is there any part of your life where you consider yourself a 'Muslim' outwardly but lack the inner conviction of a believer? What step will you take to align them?

Refuting the Muwafat View: Present Faith is Real
Refutation of muwafat view and proof of present faith via Quran and practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the view that only the state at death matters (muwafat) is false and how the Quran affirms the reality of present faith.

Core Idea
Present faith is real and recognized by Allah, not just a future hope.

This lesson tackles a key debate about the nature of faith: is it only valid at death, or is it real here and now? The author refutes the muwafat view, arguing that the Quran itself treats believers' current faith as genuine and uses it as the basis for rulings. We'll see the evidence from verses and the logical flaw in the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Understand the muwafat view
Grasp the position that only the final state at death matters, making present faith uncertain. The author notes that proponents do not deny present affirmation (tasdiq), but they withhold judgment due to the unknown end.
This view creates doubt about one's current state of faith.
2
See the refutation
The author argues that since the final state is unknown, the muwafat view leads to ignorance of one's present state. He then provides Quranic proofs that treat present faith as valid.
The refutation relies on the Quran's explicit language.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Three pieces of evidence: Allah testifies to the faith of believers (verse 2:285), praises those who respond to the call of faith without exception (3:193), and commands saying 'We believe' without qualification (2:136).
None of these verses include an exception based on the final state.
4
Reflect on practical rulings
The author notes that Islamic rulings on worship and permissibility use the name of faith without hesitation, indicating that present faith is the basis for these rulings.
This shows that the Shariah itself treats present faith as definitive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان مؤمنا عند الله حقيقة، وإنما الشك أن يكون مؤمنا وقت الموت ولا يظن بهم أنهم يشكون في وجود التصديق منهم للحال بل إنما يثبتون ذلك على القول بالموافاة وهو أن المذهب عندهم أن لا عبرة للإيمان الموجود للحال ولا للكفر الموجود للحال بل العبرة بحالة الموت وتلك الحالة مستورة عليهم، فإذا لم يعلموا بها لا يعلمون ما هم عليه للحال لسقوط اعتبار ما هو الموجود للحال، وبمعرفة بطلان ذلك يعرف بطلان هذا، والذي يدل على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه أن الله تعالى شهد بالإيمان لمن آمن بالله ورسله بقوله تعالى: آمَنَ الرَّسُولُ بِمَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْهِ مِن رَّبِّهِ وَالْمُؤْمِنُونَ ومدح بقطع القول الذين قالوا: رَبَّنَا إِنَّنَا سَمِعْنَا مُنَادِيًا يُنَادِي لِلْإِيمَانِ أَنْ آمِنُوا بِرَبِّكُمْ فَآمَنَّا الآية ولم يأمر بالاستثناء وإن لم يكن لهم بالعاقبة علم، وأمر أيضا بالقول بذلك من غير الاستثناء بقوله تعالى: قُولُوا آمَنَّا ثم خاطب الله تعالى خلقه في كثير من العبادات باسم الإيمان وفي كثير من الحل والحرمة ثم لم أحد تحرج في شيء مما أحل باسم الإيمان وأمر به ظنًا منه بنفسه أنه ليس يوجد بحقيق لذلك الاسم وأن المراد ينصرف إلى غيره فكذا التسمي به، والله الموفق.
He was a believer before Allah in reality, and the doubt is only that he might be a believer at the time of death. And it is not thought of them that they doubt the existence of affirmation (tasdiq) from them at present; rather they only affirm that according to the position of muwafat, which is that the school with them is that no consideration is given to the faith existing at present nor to the disbelief existing at present; rather consideration is given to the state of death, and that state is hidden from them. So if they do not know it, they do not know what they are upon at present due to the fall of consideration of what exists at present. And by knowing the falsehood of that, the falsehood of this becomes known. And that which indicates the correctness of what we have gone to is that Allah the Exalted testified to faith for those who believe in Allah and His messengers by His saying: 'The Messenger believes in what was revealed to him from his Lord, and the believers' and He praised those who said definitively: 'Our Lord, indeed we have heard a caller calling to faith, saying: Believe in your Lord, and we have believed' – the verse – and He did not command exception, even though they had no knowledge of the final outcome. And He also commanded saying that without exception by His saying: 'Say: We believe.' Then Allah the Exalted addressed His creation in many acts of worship with the name of faith, and in many matters of permissibility and prohibition. Then no one hesitated in anything that was made permissible by the name of faith and commanded by it, thinking himself that he does not truly exist for that name and that the meaning refers to something else, so likewise naming with it. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1100

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that only the state at death (muwafat) determines one's true faith. The author argues that present faith is real and valid. He notes that the doubters do not deny that believers have present affirmation (tasdiq); rather they claim that only the final state matters. But since that state is unknown, they cannot judge present faith. The author then provides Quranic evidence: Allah testifies to the faith of believers in the verse about the Messenger and the believers, and He praises those who responded to the call of faith without any exception. Allah also commands believers to say 'We believe' without qualification (istithna). This shows that present faith is genuine and recognized by Allah. Moreover, in many rulings of worship and permissibility, the name of faith is used, and no one hesitates to apply that name to themselves, thinking that they might not truly deserve it. Thus, the author concludes that naming oneself as a believer is valid and that the muwafat view is false.

التصديق
الاستثناء

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only the state at death determines true faith; present faith is uncertain and not real.
Correction: The Quran affirms present faith as genuine, and the Shariah bases rulings on it without requiring knowledge of the final state.

Checkpoint

A) That the Quran commands believers to say 'we believe' without exception
B) That faith is only valid at death
C) That believers should never affirm faith

Key Takeaway
The Quran affirms present faith as genuine, negating the muwafat view that only the final state matters.

Do you apply the name of believer to yourself fully when it comes to acting on your faith, or do you hold back? What would change if you lived as if your present faith is truly acknowledged by Allah?

The Identity of Islam and Iman as Tasdiq
Nasafi declares Islam and Iman synonymous under tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that when faith (iman) is defined as affirmation (tasdiq), it becomes identical to Islam (islam), and both terms refer to the same reality of submission and acknowledgment of tawhid.

Core Idea
When iman is defined as tasdiq, Islam and iman are synonymous.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a key question in Islamic theology: Are Islam and iman the same or different? He argues that once we define iman as tasdiq (affirmation), the two become identical. This resolves a common confusion and shows that the core of both is submission to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the author's clear declaration that Islam and iman do not differ.
2
Identify the Main Claim
The claim is that Islam and iman are one thing, and the names are synonymous. Find the sentence where this is stated.
3
Understand the Reasoning
The reasoning is: iman is tasdiq (affirmation) and islam is surrender, but both point to the same reality—complete submission to and affirmation of Allah's oneness.
The author uses the phrases 'شهادة العقول والآيات والآثار' and 'إسلام المرء نفسه بكليتها'.
4
Apply the Conclusion
Reflect on the implication: every believer (mu'min) is a muslim and every muslim is a believer (mu'min). This unifies the concepts at a fundamental level.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإسلام والإيمان لا يتغايران وإذا عرف أن الإيمان هو التصديق عرفنا أن الإيمان والإسلام شيء واحد، والأسماء من قبيل الأسماء المترادفة، وكل مؤمن مسلم وكل مسلم مؤمن، وذلك لأن الإيمان اسم لتصديق شهادة العقول والآيات والآثار على وحدانية الله تعالى، وأن له الخلق والأمر ولا شريك له في ذلك، والإسلام هو إسلام المرء نفسه بكليتها، وكذا كل شيء بالعبودية لله تعالى لا شريك له فحصلا عن طريق المراد منهما على واحد.
Islam and Iman do not differ. And when it is known that iman is tasdiq (affirmation), we know that iman and islam are one thing, and these names are of the type of synonymous names. And every believer (mu'min) is a muslim, and every muslim is a believer (mu'min). That is because iman is a name for the affirmation (tasdiq) of the testimony of intellects, signs, and traditions upon the oneness of Allah the Exalted, and that He has creation and command, and no partner has He in that. And islam is the surrender (islam) of one's entire self, and likewise everything in servitude to Allah the Exalted, who has no partner. So they yield, from the standpoint of what is intended from them, one thing.
Source pages p. 1100

Commentary
This passage is a definition and identification. The author first states that iman and islam are not different (لا يتغايران). Then he explains that once iman is defined as tasdiq (affirmation), it becomes clear that iman and islam are one and the same. He categorizes them as synonymous terms (أسماء مترادفة). The reasoning is that iman is the affirmation of the testimony of intellects, revealed signs (ayat), and transmitted reports (athar) concerning the oneness of Allah and that He alone has creation and command. Islam, on the other hand, is the surrender of one's entire self and everything in servitude to Allah, without any partner. Since both iman and islam ultimately point to the same reality—complete submission and affirmation of tawhid—they are considered one and the same thing.

Key Terms
التصديق
المترادفة
الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Islam and Iman are different in all contexts.
Correction: This passage shows they are identical when iman is understood as tasdiq, and the names are synonymous.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the relationship between iman and islam?
A) They are different
B) They are synonymous
C) Islam is part of iman
D) Iman is part of islam

Key Takeaway
Iman and Islam are the same when iman is defined as tasdiq, because both entail complete submission and affirmation of Allah's oneness.

Islam Linguistically Means Sincerity (Ikhlas)
The author argues linguistically that islam means sincerity, equating it with iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic argument that islam means sincerity (ikhlas) and how it supports the unity of islam and iman.

Core Idea
Islam linguistically means sincerity – the same inner reality as iman.

This passage presents a key linguistic argument from the Qur'an. The author shows that the word 'islam' in Arabic is rooted in sincerity (ikhlas), and that this meaning is confirmed by the story of Prophet Ibrahim. Before we examine the passage, consider: what does it mean to submit? Is it just outward actions, or something deeper?

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the author cites two Quranic verses.
2
Understand the linguistic claim
The author states that 'islam' in the language means 'ikhlas' (sincerity). This is the core claim.
Ikhlas is the state of being pure and exclusive in devotion.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
First verse: Allah commands Ibrahim 'aslim' (submit) and Ibrahim replies 'aslamtu' (I have submitted), interpreted as 'I have become sincere.' Second verse: a longer verse where believers affirm faith in all prophets and conclude 'we are to Him muslims.'
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that islam is the servant's sincerity in devoting himself entirely to Allah without partners. This meaning returns to the earlier explanation that islam and iman are one and the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل: الإسلام في اللغة هو الإخلاص على ما قال تعالى لإبراهيم الخليل: أَسْلِمْ قَالَ أَسْلَمْتُ أي أخلص، قال أخلصت ومن قوله تعالى: وَآمَنَّا بِاللَّهِ وَمَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْنَا وَمَا أُنزِلَ إِلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَاعِيلَ وَإِسْحَاقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ وَالْأَسْبَاطِ وَمَا أُوتِيَ مُوسَى وَعِيسَى وَمَا أُوتِيَ النَّبِيُّونَ مِن رَّبِّهِمْ لا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ وَنَحْنُ لَهُ مُسْلِمُونَ فهو على إخلاص العبد نفسه الله تعالى لا يجعل فيه شركاء، وهو أيضا يرجع إلى ما بينا.
And it is said: Islam in the language is sincerity (ikhlas), according to what Allah the Exalted said to Ibrahim al-Khalil: 'Submit (aslim)' he said: 'I have submitted (aslamtu)' meaning 'I have become sincere' – he said 'I have become sincere.' And from His saying: 'And we believe in Allah and what was revealed to us and what was revealed to Ibrahim, Isma'il, Ishaq, Ya'qub, and the tribes, and what was given to Musa, Isa, and what was given to the prophets from their Lord; we make no distinction between any of them, and to Him we are muslims (submitting ones).' So it (islam) is based on the servant's sincerity of himself to Allah, he does not make partners in it. And it also returns to what we have explained.
Source pages p. 1101

Commentary
This passage provides a linguistic argument for the identity of islam and iman. The author reports a saying that islam linguistically means ikhlas (sincerity). He supports this with the Quranic verse where Allah commands Ibrahim: 'Aslim' (Submit), and Ibrahim replies 'Aslamtu' (I have submitted), which is interpreted as 'I have become sincere.' Then he quotes a longer verse where believers declare their faith in all prophets and conclude 'and we are to Him muslims' (submitting ones). This shows that islam is the servant's sincerity in devoting himself entirely to Allah without any partners. The author concludes that this meaning also returns to what he had previously explained about iman and islam being one and the same.

Key Terms
الإخلاص
الإسلام
أَسْلِمْ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That islam is only about external actions and rituals, without inner sincerity.
Correction: This passage shows that islam linguistically means sincerity (ikhlas), indicating that true submission involves inner devotion and sincerity to Allah alone.

Checkpoint
What linguistic evidence does the author use to connect islam and iman?
A) The definition of iman
B) The Quranic command to 'aslim' meaning ikhlas
C) The hadith of Jibril
D) The consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Islam linguistically means sincerity (ikhlas), and this shows that true submission is an inner state of devotion to Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a Muslim,' do you think of it as an outward label or as a deep inner reality of sincerity (ikhlas) to Allah? What would change in your life if you lived every action as an expression of that inner sincerity?
?
Ibrahim's entire being replied 'aslamtu' — a pure, unquestioning submission. In which areas of your life do you hold back from submitting fully to Allah? What is one specific step you will take this week to transform that area into sincere submission?
?
If someone observed your daily actions, would they see that your submission to Allah is a matter of inner devotion without any partners? Where might you be 'associating' other motives — such as people-pleasing, status, or comfort — with your worship? How can you purify your intention starting today?

Hashwiyya Argument: Iman and Islam Are Different
Nasafi presents the Hashwiyya's proof that iman and islam are distinct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hashwiyya's two proofs for distinguishing iman and islam and how they use Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
The Hashwiyya use Quran and hadith to argue iman and islam are distinct.

In this passage, al-Nasafi presents the argument of the Hashwiyya, a group that insisted on a sharp distinction between iman (faith) and islam (submission). They bring two scriptural evidences: a Quranic verse and the famous hadith of Gabriel. Understanding their reasoning is essential for grasping the broader kalam debate on the relationship between faith and actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic source passage and its English translation to get a sense of the argument.
Pay attention to the structure of the argument.
2
Identify the two proofs
Notice the two separate arguments: the Quranic verse and the Gabriel hadith. See how each is used to show a difference between iman and islam.
3
Consider the implications
Think about what it means if iman and islam are distinct. This sets up the refutation in subsequent lessons.
This argument challenges the Maturidi view that iman and islam are essentially the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم بعض الحشوية أن الإيمان غير الإسلام واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: (قَالَتِ الْأَعْرَابُ امَنَّا قُل لَّمْ تُؤْمِنُوا وَلَكِن قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا) جعل الإسلام غير الإيمان حيث أثبت الإسلام ونفى الإيمان، واحتجوا أيضا بخبر جبريل عليه السلام فإنه سأل النبي عن الإيمان فقال: "أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر والقدر خيره وشره - من الله - وسأل عن الإسلام فقال: أن تشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وتقيم الصلاة وتؤتي الزكاة وتصوم رمضان وتحج البيت فقال في الأول: إذا فعلت كذا فأنا مؤمن وفي الثاني فأنا مسلم قال : نعم. قال: صدقت ففرق الكتاب والسنة بين الأمرين.
And some of the Hashwiyya claimed that iman is other than islam, and they argued by His saying: 'The Bedouins say: We believe. Say: You do not believe, but say: We have submitted (aslamna).' He made islam other than iman, where He affirmed islam and negated iman. And they also argued by the hadith of Gabriel, peace be upon him, for he asked the Prophet about iman, and he said: 'That you believe in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and the divine decree, its good and evil – from Allah.' And he asked about islam, and he said: 'That you testify that there is no god but Allah, establish prayer, give zakat, fast Ramadan, and perform hajj to the House.' He said in the first: 'If you do such, then I am a believer,' and in the second: 'Then I am a Muslim.' He said: 'Yes.' He said: 'You have spoken the truth.' So the Book and the Sunnah distinguished between the two matters.
Source pages p. 1101

Commentary
This passage presents the argument of the Hashwiyya (a term for anthropomorphist or literalist groups) who assert that iman (faith) and islam (submission) are distinct. They provide two proofs. First, the Quranic verse (49:14) where Allah tells the Bedouins not to say 'we believe' but to say 'we have submitted,' thereby affirming islam while denying iman. Second, the well-known hadith of Gabriel where the Prophet defines iman as belief in Allah, angels, books, messengers, Last Day, and decree, and defines islam as the five pillars (shahada, prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj). In the hadith, the Prophet affirms that performing these actions makes one a Muslim, and believing the articles makes one a believer. The Hashwiyya conclude that the Book and Sunnah differentiate between the two, so they are not identical.

Key Terms
الحشوية
الإيمان
الإسلام
الحديث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hashwiyya believe that the Quran and hadith prove iman and islam are completely distinct and separate.
Correction: The verse and hadith actually show a relationship and difference in definition, but not necessarily a separation in reality; the Maturidi view holds that iman and islam are intimately connected.

Checkpoint
What are the two proofs the Hashwiyya use to argue that iman and islam are different?
A) Quran verse 49:14 and the hadith of Gabriel
B) Quran verse 2:136 and the hadith of the Prophet's migration
C) Quran verse 3:19 and the hadith of the Night Journey
D) Quran verse 2:131 and the hadith of the Prophet's farewell

Key Takeaway
The Hashwiyya argue that iman and islam are distinct based on the Bedouins verse and the Gabriel hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, do you ever content yourself with the outward acts of islam while your heart is far from true iman? What specific area of your faith feels more like a routine than a belief?
?
If iman and islam were truly separate, would you be satisfied being merely a Muslim without deeper faith? What would you do today to ensure your submission is accompanied by genuine conviction?
?
The Hashwiyya used the Bedouins verse to argue that one can be a Muslim without being a believer. Do you ever rely on your rituals to feel secure, ignoring the state of your heart? How will you check your iman this week, not just your islam?

Nasafi's Logical Argument: Iman and Islam Are One
Nasafi presents the logical proof for the identity of iman and islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's logical proof that iman and islam are the same reality and cannot be separated.

Core Idea
Iman and Islam are synonyms—you cannot have one without the other.

Nasafi begins by reiterating his definition that the reality of iman and islam is identical. He then presents a powerful logical argument: it is impossible for someone to fulfill all conditions of iman yet not be a Muslim, or vice versa. This establishes that they are two names for one reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting Nasafi's definition and the logical impossibility he presents.
2
Understand the analogy
Nasafi compares iman and islam to synonyms like 'sitting' and 'sitting'. Reflect on why this refutes the Hashwiyya view.
3
Ask the key question
If iman and islam were distinct, could a person be a believer without being a Muslim? Use Nasafi's argument to answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنا أنا حقيقة الإيمان والإسلام لما كانا ما ذكرنا كان وجود أحدهما الآخر محالاً، إذ هي جميعًا اسم لشيء واحد كالقعود والجلوس، يوضحه أن من البعيد عن العقول أن يأتي المرء بجميع شرائط الإيمان ثم لا يكون مسلماً أو يأتي بجميع شرائط الإسلام ثم لا يكون مؤمنا يدل عليه أن الله تعالى قال: ﴿ إِنَّ الدِّين عِندَ اللَّهِ الْإِسْلَامُ ﴾ وقال: ﴿ وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ ﴾ والإيمان دين فلو كان غير الإسلام لكان ينبغي أن لا يقبل. وقال تعالى: ﴿ فَأَخْرَجْنَا مَن كَانَ فِيهَا مِنَ المُؤْمِنِينَ فَمَا وَجَدْنَا فِيهَا غَيْرَ بَيْتٍ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ ﴾ وقال تعالى: ﴿ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا بِايَتِنَا وَكَانُوا مُسْلِمِينَ ﴾ وقال خبرا عن موسى عليه السلام أنه قال لقومه : يَقَوْمٍ إِن كُنتُمْ امَنتُم بِاللَّهِ فعَليْهِ تَوَكَّلُوا إِن كُنتُم مُّسْلِمِينَ ﴾ وقال : ﴿ إِن تُسْمِعُ إِلَّا مَن يُؤْمِنُ بِايَتِنَا فَهُم مُّسْلِمُونَ ﴾ وقال : ﴿ يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا اتَّقُوا اللهَ حَقَّ تُقَائِهِ وَلَا تَمُوتُنَّ إِلَّا وَأَنتُم مُّسْلِمُونَ ﴾ وقال: ﴿ قُولُوا مَا مَنَا بِاللَّهِ وَمَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْنَا وَمَا أُنزِلَ إِلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَعِيلَ وَإِسْحَاقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ وَالْأَسْبَاطِ وَمَا أُوتِيَ مُوسَى وَعِيسَى وَمَا أُوتِيَ النَّبِيُّونَ مِن رَّبِّهِمْ لَا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ وَنَحْنُ لَهُ مُسْلِمُونَ ﴾ فأمرهم في أول الآية أن يقولوا : ( وَامَنَا ) ثم ختم الآية بأن قال: قولوا أنا مسلمون" ثم قال: ﴿ فَإنّ ءَامَنُوا بِمِثْلِ مَا ءَامَنتُم بِهِ فَقَدِ اهْتَدَوا ﴾ وقال في آية أخرى: ﴿ وَقُل لِلَّذِينَ أُوتُوا
And we have that the reality of iman and islam, since they are what we mentioned, the existence of one without the other is impossible, because they are both names for one thing, like sitting and sitting [synonyms]. This is clarified by the fact that it is far from reason that a person should fulfill all the conditions of iman and then not be a Muslim, or fulfill all the conditions of islam and then not be a believer. Evidence for that is that Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, the religion in the sight of Allah is Islam.' And He said: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him.' And iman is a religion, so if it were other than islam, it would be necessary that it not be accepted. And He said: 'And We brought out from there the believers, and We found not there other than a single house of Muslims.' And He said: 'Those who believed in Our signs and were Muslims.' And He said, telling of Moses, peace be upon him, that he said to his people: 'O my people, if you have believed in Allah, then rely upon Him, if you are Muslims.' And He said: 'You cannot make hear except those who believe in Our signs, so they are Muslims.' And He said: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah as He should be feared, and do not die except as Muslims.' And He said: 'Say: We believe in Allah and what has been sent down to us and what has been sent down to Abraham, Ishmael, Isaac, Jacob, and the tribes, and what was given to Moses and Jesus and what was given to the prophets from their Lord. We do not distinguish between any of them, and we are Muslims to Him.' So He commanded them at the beginning of the verse to say 'we believe,' then ended the verse by saying: say 'we are Muslims.' Then He said: 'So if they believe in the like of what you believe in, then they are guided.' And He said in another verse: 'And say to those who were given...'
Source pages p. 1102

Commentary
This passage contains Nasafi's refutation of the Hashwiyya position. He begins by stating his previous definition: the reality of iman and islam being one, it is impossible for one to exist without the other. They are like synonyms (e.g., 'sitting' and 'sitting'). It is unreasonable that someone could fulfill all conditions of iman yet not be a Muslim, or vice versa. Then he provides extensive Quranic evidence. First, Surah Al-Imran (3:19) states that the religion with Allah is islam, and (3:85) says any other religion is not accepted. Since iman is a religion, if it were different from islam, it would not be accepted. Second, Surah Adh-Dhariyat (51:35-36) equates believers with Muslims, finding no Muslim house except that of believers. Third, Surah Az-Zukhruf (43:69) couples belief in signs with being Muslims. Fourth, Surah Yunus (10:84) has Moses telling those who believe to rely on Allah if they are Muslims, linking the two. Fifth, Surah An-Naml (27:81) states that only those who believe in signs are Muslims. Sixth, Surah Al-Imran (3:102) commands believers to die as Muslims. Seventh, Surah Al-Baqarah (2:136) initially says 'say: we believe' and concludes 'we are Muslims,' showing interchangeability. The verse (2:137) further states that if they believe as you believe, they are guided. Thus, the Quran consistently treats iman and islam as synonymous.

Key Terms
الإيمان (iman)
الإسلام (islam)
الشرائط (conditions)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman and Islam are distinct and can exist independently.
Correction: Nasafi argues they are synonyms like sitting and sitting; it is impossible to have one without the other.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the relationship between iman and islam?
A) They are distinct and can exist separately.
B) They are synonyms and cannot be separated.
C) One is a subset of the other.
D) They are unrelated.

Key Takeaway
Iman and Islam are two names for the same reality; you cannot be a believer without being a Muslim.

Quranic Evidence for the Identity of Iman and Islam
Nasafi cites Quranic verses that equate iman and islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses multiple Quranic verses to prove that iman and islam are identical.

Core Idea
The Quran consistently treats 'iman' and 'islam' as interchangeable.

After establishing the logical argument, Nasafi provides a cascade of Quranic evidence. Each verse either equates believers with Muslims or implies that the two terms refer to the same reality. This reinforces his claim against the Hashwiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses in order
Read each Quranic citation carefully, noting how it connects iman and islam.
2
Identify the pattern
Notice that in each verse, believers are called Muslims, or faith is linked to being Muslim. This shows they are the same.
3
Reflect on the cumulative effect
Consider why Nasafi lists so many verses. How does the multiplicity strengthen his argument?

And we have that the reality of iman and islam, since they are what we mentioned, the existence of one without the other is impossible, because they are both names for one thing, like sitting and sitting [synonyms]. First, Surah Al-Imran (3:19) states that the religion with Allah is islam, and (3:85) says any other religion is not accepted. Since iman is a religion, if it were different from islam, it would not be accepted. Second, Surah Adh-Dhariyat (51:35-36) equates believers with Muslims, finding no Muslim house except that of believers. Third, Surah Az-Zukhruf (43:69) couples belief in signs with being Muslims. Fourth, Surah Yunus (10:84) has Moses telling those who believe to rely on Allah if they are Muslims, linking the two. Fifth, Surah An-Naml (27:81) states that only those who believe in signs are Muslims. Sixth, Surah Al-Imran (3:102) commands believers to die as Muslims. Seventh, Surah Al-Baqarah (2:136) initially says 'say: we believe' and concludes 'we are Muslims,' showing interchangeability. The verse (2:137) further states that if they believe as you believe, they are guided. Thus, the Quran consistently treats iman and islam as synonymous.

Key Terms
الإيمان (iman)
الإسلام (islam)
الدين (religion)
الآيات (verses)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does Nasafi use to argue that if iman were different from islam, it would not be accepted?
A) 3:19 or 3:85
B) 51:35-36
C) 2:136
D) 27:81

Key Takeaway
The Quran repeatedly equates iman and islam, showing they are one reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if your iman and islam are the same reality, or do you compartmentalize your faith and actions, allowing a gap between what you believe and how you submit? This lesson demands consistency. What specific area of your life will you work on today to eliminate that gap?
?
When you sin or neglect an obligation, do you feel that your iman is intact even if your islam is weak? The Quran ties them together. How can you hold yourself accountable so that your belief transforms into submission, not just in theory but in your daily decisions?
?
The verses command believers to die as Muslims. Are you living each moment with that end in mind, or are you assuming your final state is secure without ensuring your present state of submission? What one habit will you change starting now to align your life with this teaching?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
12 min
Al-Nasafi's Proof that Islam and Iman Are Identical
Al-Nasafi proves Islam and Iman are identical using Quranic verses and addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi proves the essential identity of Islam and Iman using rational analogy, extensive Quranic evidence, and a rebuttal to the objection that they could be separate.

Core Idea
Islam and Iman are two names for the same reality.

In this passage, al-Nasafi argues forcefully that Islam and Iman are not two separate components of religion but refer to the same essential reality. He begins with a rational argument and then marshals an extensive array of Quranic verses to show that the two terms are used interchangeably. Finally, he confronts the potential objection that if they were distinct, one could exist without the other, challenging his opponents to make sense of that consequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening thesis
Start by reading the first few lines where al-Nasafi states that the existence of one without the other is impossible, giving the analogy of sitting and squatting.
This sets the foundation for the entire argument.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
List the Quranic verses al-Nasafi cites. Notice how each verse either equates or closely associates Iman and Islam.
He uses over a dozen verses to build cumulative evidence.
3
Consider the hadith
Read the hadith about entering Paradise only as a believer or as a Muslim. This reinforces the interchangeability.
4
Analyze the objection and rebuttal
Al-Nasafi challenges his opponents: if Iman and Islam are distinct, we could conceive a believer who is not a Muslim. He asks them to categorize such a person.
This shows the logical absurdity of separating them.
5
Synthesize the argument
Reflect on how rational reasoning and scriptural evidence together establish that Iman and Islam are identical.
This is a classic Maturidi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنا أنا حقيقة الإيمان والإسلام لما كانا ما ذكرنا كان وجود أحدهما الآخر محالاً، إذ هي جميعًا اسم لشيء واحد كالقعود والجلوس، يوضحه أن من البعيد عن العقول أن يأتي المرء بجميع شرائط الإيمان ثم لا يكون مسلمًا أو يأتي بجميع شرائط الإسلام ثم لا يكون مؤمنا يدل عليه أن الله تعالى قال: ﴿ إِنَّ الدِّين عِندَ اللَّهِ الْإِسْلَامُ ﴾ وقال: ﴿ وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ ﴾ والإيمان دين فلو كان غير الإسلام لكان ينبغي أن لا يقبل. وقال تعالى: ﴿ فَأَخْرَجْنَا مَن كَانَ فِيهَا مِنَ المُؤْمِنِينَ فَمَا وَجَدْنَا فِيهَا غَيْرَ بَيْتٍ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ ﴾ وقال تعالى: ﴿ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا بِايَتِنَا وَكَانُوا مُسْلِمِينَ ﴾ وقال خبرا عن موسى عليه السلام أنه قال لقومه : يَقَوْمٍ إِن كُنتُمْ امَنتُم بِاللَّهِ فعَليْهِ تَوَكَّلُوا إِن كُنتُم مُّسْلِمِينَ ﴾ وقال : إِن تُسْمِعُ إِلَّا مَن يُؤْمِنُ بِايَتِنَا فَهُم مُّسْلِمُونَ ﴾ وقال : يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا اتَّقُوا اللهَ حَقَّ تُقَائِهِ وَلَا تَمُوتُنَّ إِلَّا وَأَنتُم مُّسْلِمُونَ ﴾ وقال: ﴿ قُولُوا مَا مَنَا بِاللَّهِ وَمَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْنَا وَمَا أُنزِلَ إِلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَعِيلَ وَإِسْحَاقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ وَالْأَسْبَاطِ وَمَا أُوتِيَ مُوسَى وَعِيسَى وَمَا أُوتِيَ النَّبِيُّونَ مِن رَّبِّهِمْ لَا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ وَنَحْنُ لَهُ مُسْلِمُونَ ﴾ فأمرهم في أول الآية أن يقولوا : ( وَامَنَا ) ثم ختم الآية بأن قال: قولوا أنا مسلمون" ثم قال: فَإنّ ءَامَنُوا بِمِثْلِ مَا ءَامَنتُم بِهِ فَقَدِ اهْتَدَوا ﴾ وقال في آية أخرى: ﴿ وَقُل لِلَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الكِتَبَ ﴿١﴾ وَالْأُمِّينَ أَسْلَمْتُمْ فَإِنْ أَسْلَمُوا فَقَدِ اهْتَدَوا ﴾ جعلهم في هذه الآية مهتدين بإسلامهم كما جعلهم في الآية الأولى مهتدين بإيمانهم، فهذا دليل واضح لا شك فيه أن جعل الإيمان والإسلام شيئًا واحدا لا يفترقان، وقال يوسف عليه السلام: تَوَفَّنِي مُسلِمًا وَالْحِقْنِي بِالصَّلِحِينَ ﴾ وغير المؤمن لا يلحق بالصالحين وقال تعالى: يَمُنُّونَ عَلَيْكَ أَنْ أَسْلَمُوا قُل لَّا تَمُنُّوا عَلَى إِسْلَامَكُم بَلِ اللَّهُ يَمُنُّ عَلَيْكُمْ أَنْ هَدَنَكُمْ لِلْإِيمَنِ إِن كُنتُمْ صدِقِينَ ﴾ وقد روى عن النبي عليه السلام أنه قال: "لا يدخل الجنة إلا نفس مؤمنة" وروى إلا نفس مسلمة ، ثم لا تنازع في جميع المسلمين أن الدار التي الأهل الإسلام هي لأهل الإيمان وأن التي هي لهؤلاء، فهي لهؤلاء وكذا الله تعالى قسم الخلق فقال: فَيَنكُمْ كَافِرٌ وَمِنكُم مُّؤْمِنٌ ﴾ وقال : يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوهٌ ﴾ فما فتوى صاحب هذا القول في المسلم أنه من أي قسم في الآيتين، ثم يقال له لو كان الاسمان اسمين لمتغايرين لتصور وجود أحدهما بدون الآخر ولتصور مؤمن ليس بمسلم ومسلم ليس بمؤمن ثم لو كان كذلك فما قولك في مؤمن ليس بمسلم
We hold that since the reality of Iman and Islam are as we have mentioned, the existence of one without the other is impossible, because both are names for one thing, like sitting and squatting. This is clarified by the fact that it is far from reason for a person to fulfill all the conditions of Iman and then not be Muslim, or to fulfill all the conditions of Islam and then not be a believer. Evidence for this is that Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, the religion in the sight of Allah is Islam.' And He said: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him.' Iman is a religion, so if it were other than Islam, it would be worthy of not being accepted. And Allah Almighty said: 'Then We brought out whoever was among the believers; and We found not therein other than a house of Muslims.' And Allah Almighty said: 'Those who believed in Our signs and were Muslims.' And He related from Moses, peace be upon him, that he said to his people: 'O my people, if you have believed in Allah, then rely upon Him, if you are Muslims.' And He said: 'You cannot make hear except those who believe in Our signs, so they are Muslims.' And He said: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah as He should be feared, and do not die except as Muslims.' And He said: 'Say, we have believed in Allah and what has been revealed to us and what was revealed to Abraham, Ishmael, Isaac, Jacob, and the tribes, and what was given to Moses and Jesus and what was given to the prophets from their Lord; we make no distinction between any of them, and we are Muslims to Him.' So He commanded them at the beginning of the verse to say 'we have believed' and then concluded the verse by saying: 'say we are Muslims.' Then He said: 'So if they believe in the like of what you have believed in, then they have been guided.' And He said in another verse: 'And say to those who were given the Scripture and the unlettered, have you submitted? Then if they submit, they have been guided.' He made them in this verse guided by their submission (Islam) just as He made them in the first verse guided by their faith (Iman). So this is clear evidence, no doubt in it, that He made Iman and Islam one thing that do not separate. And Joseph, peace be upon him, said: 'Cause me to die a Muslim and join me with the righteous.' And the non-believer is not joined with the righteous. And Allah Almighty said: 'They consider it a favor to you that they have submitted. Say, do not consider your submission a favor to me; rather, Allah confers favor upon you that He has guided you to Iman, if you are truthful.' And it has been narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'None enters Paradise except a believing soul,' and it was narrated: 'except a Muslim soul.' Then there is no dispute among all Muslims that the abode whose people are Muslims belongs to the people of Iman, and that whatever is for these is for those. Likewise, Allah Almighty divided creation, saying: 'And among you are disbelievers and among you are believers' and said: 'On the Day when faces become white and faces become black.' So what is the verdict of the holder of this view regarding the Muslim: which category is he in the two verses? Then it is said to him: if the two names were names for two different things, then the existence of one without the other would be conceivable, and it would be conceivable to have a believer who is not a Muslim and a Muslim who is not a believer. Then, if so, what do you say about a believer who is not a Muslim?
Source pages p. 1102

Commentary
This passage presents al-Nasafi's proof that Islam and Iman (faith) are identical in meaning, not two distinct concepts. The author begins by stating his thesis: since the true nature of Iman and Islam is as previously established (both being inward affirmation and outward submission), it is impossible for one to exist without the other. He compares them to 'sitting' and 'squatting' — two words for essentially the same action. He then argues that it is rationally unacceptable for a person to fulfill all conditions of Iman and not be Muslim, or vice versa. To support this, he cites numerous Quranic verses that use 'Iman' and 'Islam' interchangeably or pair them together. For example, verse 3:19 declares that the religion is Islam, and verse 3:85 warns that any other religion will not be accepted — since Iman is a religion, if it were different from Islam, it would not be accepted. Other verses (51:35-36, 43:69, 10:84, 27:81, 3:102, 2:136-137, 3:20) similarly equate or closely associate the two terms. Al-Nasafi highlights that in 2:136, Allah commands the believers to say 'we have believed' (āmnnā) and then 'we are Muslims,' and in 2:137, guidance is linked to believing 'in the like of what you have believed in.' In 3:20, guidance is linked to submission (aslamtum). Thus, guidance is attributed to both Iman and Islam, proving they are one. He also cites the supplication of Joseph (12:101) asking to die a Muslim and be joined with the righteous — implying that a non-believer (ghayr al-mu'min) cannot be righteous. Further, verse 49:17 shows that guidance to Iman is a favor, linking it to Islam. The author then mentions a hadith that 'none enters Paradise except a believing soul' and another version 'except a Muslim soul,' showing interchangeability. Finally, he addresses an objection: if the two terms were distinct, one could exist without the other — we could conceive of a believer who is not a Muslim or a Muslim who is not a believer. He challenges the opponent to categorize such a person. The overall argument is a comprehensive scriptural proof for the Maturidi position that Iman and Islam are synonymous in the sense that true Iman necessarily entails outward submission (Islam), and vice versa, focusing on the essential unity of the religion.

Key Terms
إيمان (Iman)
إسلام (Islam)
دين (religion)
مسلم (Muslim)
مؤمن (believer)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman and Islam are separate entities that can exist independently.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues they are identical in meaning, and their separation is inconceivable based on rational and scriptural evidence.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi's argument in this passage, what would be the consequence if Iman and Islam were two distinct things?
A) A person could be a Muslim without being a believer.
B) A person could be a believer without being a Muslim.
C) Both A and B would be conceivable.
D) Neither A nor B would be possible.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi proves that Iman and Islam are one reality using rational analogy and cumulative Quranic evidence, dismissing the possibility of their separation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Nasafi insists that Iman and Islam are identical, meaning your belief and your submission cannot be separated. In your daily life, where do you see a gap between what you claim to believe and how you actually live? What would change if you truly treated them as one reality?
?
Verse 49:17 reminds you that guidance to Iman is a favor from Allah. When was the last time you sincerely thanked Allah for guiding you to this faith—not in general terms, but with specific gratitude for the ability to believe and submit? What would it look like to live each day conscious that your Iman is a gift?
?
The analogy of 'sitting and squatting' shows that different words can refer to the same action. Are there areas of your life where you say 'I believe' but act as if submission is optional? What step will you take today to close that gap and make your belief and practice one?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
