Scriptural Proofs for the Identity of Iman and Islam
The author cites three Quranic verses and a hadith to prove iman and islam are identical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran and Sunnah demonstrate that iman (faith) and islam (submission) are synonymous and not distinct categories.

Core Idea
The Quran and Hadith prove that iman and islam are one reality.

To establish the identity of iman and islam, the author of Tabṣirat al-Adilla first turns to the primary sources. He cites three Quranic passages and a prophetic hadith that apply the same terms of guidance and reward to both, demonstrating that they are not distinct entities. This lesson walks through each proof and explains its logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the scriptural evidence
Read the Arabic passage containing three Quranic verses and a hadith once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the literal meaning.
The verses are from Surah Al-Imran, Surah Yusuf, and Surah Al-Hujurat.
2
Identify each proof
Note each proof individually: the verse from Surah Al-Imran (3:20), the prayer of Prophet Yusuf, the verse from Surah Al-Hujurat (49:17), and the prophetic hadith.
Each proof links guidance or reward to both iman and islam interchangeably.
3
Analyze the logical connection
For each proof, notice how the author argues that the same outcome (guidance, being joined with the righteous, entering Paradise) is attached to both iman and islam, implying they are the same.
This is a direct refutation of those who claim iman and islam are different.
4
Reflect on the hadith
The hadith is narrated in two versions: 'believing soul' and 'Muslim soul', showing the Prophet used them interchangeably.
This provides strong sunnah evidence for the identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكِتَابَ وَالْأُمِّينَ أَسْلَمْتُمْ فَإِنْ أَسْلَمُوا فَقَدِ اهْتَدَوا جعلهم في هذه الآية مهتدين بإسلامهم كما جعلهم في الآية الأولى مهتدين بإيمانهم، فهذا دليل واضح لا شك فيه أن جعل الإيمان والإسلام شيئًا واحدا لا يفترقان، وقال يوسف عليه السلام: تَوَفَّنِي مُسلِمًا وَالْحِقْنِي بِالصَّلِحِينَ وغير المؤمن لا يلحق بالصالحين وقال تعالى: يَمُنُّونَ عَلَيْكَ أَنْ أَسْلَمُوا قُل لَّا تَمُنُّوا عَلَى إِسْلَامَكُم بَلِ اللَّهُ يَمُنُّ عَلَيْكُمْ أَنْ هَدَنَكُمْ لِلْإِيمَنِ إِن كُنتُمْ صدِقِينَ وقد روى عن النبي عليه السلام أنه قال: "لا يدخل الجنة إلا نفس مؤمنة وروى إلا نفس مسلمة، ثم لا تنازع في جميع المسلمين أن الدار التي الأهل الإسلام هي لأهل الإيمان وأن التي هي لهؤلاء، فهي لهؤلاء وكذا الله تعالى قسم الخلق فقال: فَمِنكُمْ كَافِرٌ وَمِنكُم مُّؤْمِنٌ وقال : يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوهٌ فما فتوى صاحب هذا القول في المسلم أنه من أي قسم في الآيتين، ثم يقال له لو كان الاسمان اسمين لمتغايرين لتصور وجود أحدهما بدون الآخر ولتصور مؤمن ليس بمسلم ومسلم ليس بمؤمن ثم لو كان كذلك فما قولك في مؤمن ليس بمسلم أو مسلم ليس بمؤمن في أحكام الدنيا والآخرة؟ فإن ثبت لأحدهما حكمًا ليس للآخر ظهر ضلالة، وإن لم يثبت ظهر بطلان قوله، ثم الناس في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كانوا على ثلاثة أصناف مؤمن وكافر ومنافق فمن أيهم كان المسلم إذ لم يكن فيهم رابع؟ فإن قالوا: كان من المؤمنين تركوا مذهبهم وإن قالوا كان من الكافرين ينبغي أن لا يقبل إلا ذلك الدين وهو الكفر أو النفاق بقوله : ( وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ ) والإيمان غيره فلا يقبل بل يقبل إما الكفر وإما النفاق والقول به كفر ظاهر، والله الموفق.
The Book and the unlettered, have you submitted? If they submit then they are guided. He made them in this verse guided by their submission (islam) just as He made them in the first verse guided by their faith (iman). So this is clear evidence, no doubt in it, that He made iman and islam one thing that do not separate. And Yusuf peace be upon him said: 'Cause me to die as a Muslim and join me with the righteous.' And the non-believer is not joined with the righteous. And He said Most High: 'They consider it a favor to you that they have submitted. Say: Do not consider your submission a favor to me; rather Allah confers favor upon you that He has guided you to faith, if you are truthful.' And it was narrated from the Prophet peace be upon him that he said: 'None shall enter Paradise except a believing soul' and it was narrated 'except a Muslim soul'. Then there is no dispute among all Muslims that the abode whose people are Islam is for the people of faith, and that which is for these is for those. Similarly, Allah Most High divided creation and said: 'Among you are disbelievers and among you are believers.' And He said: 'On the day when faces become white and faces become black.' So what is the verdict of the proponent of this view concerning the Muslim: from which group is he in the two verses? Then it is said to him: If the two names were two distinct names, it would be conceivable for one to exist without the other, and it would be conceivable for a believer not to be a Muslim and a Muslim not to be a believer. Then if that were so, what do you say about a believer who is not a Muslim or a Muslim who is not a believer regarding the rulings of this world and the Hereafter? If a ruling is established for one that is not for the other, his error becomes apparent; and if it is not established, the invalidity of his statement becomes apparent. Then the people at the time of the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him were of three types: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite. From which of them was the Muslim, since there was no fourth? If they say: He was among the believers, they abandon their position; if they say he was among the disbelievers, then no religion should be accepted except that religion, which is disbelief or hypocrisy, by His saying: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him.' And iman is other than it, so it would not be accepted; rather either disbelief or hypocrisy is accepted. And this statement is manifest disbelief. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1103

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument for the identity of iman and islam, using Quranic verses, a prophetic hadith, and logical reasoning. The author begins by citing Quran 3:20 where Allah says to the People of the Book and the unlettered: 'If they submit (aslamu) then they are guided.' The author notes that in this verse guidance is linked to submission (islam), just as in another verse guidance is linked to faith (iman). This shows that iman and islam are the same. Then the author cites the Prophet Yusuf's prayer to die as a Muslim, arguing that only a believer is joined with the righteous, implying that islam equals iman. Next, Quran 49:17 is quoted, where the Bedouins think their submission (islam) is a favor, but Allah says He guided them to faith (iman). This shows that islam leads to iman, but the verse treats them as essentially the same in context. Then a hadith is cited: 'None shall enter Paradise except a believing soul' and also narrated as 'except a Muslim soul', indicating interchangeable usage. Then the author argues that there is no dispute among Muslims that Paradise is for Muslims, which is also for believers. Also, Quran 64:2 divides people into disbelievers and believers, not a separate category for Muslims. Similarly, Quran 3:106 speaks of faces turning white and black, implying two groups only. So the proponent of the distinction is asked: which group does the Muslim belong to? Then a reductio ad absurdum is presented: if iman and islam are distinct, it should be possible for a believer to not be a Muslim and vice versa, but in the rulings of this world and the Hereafter, no distinction is made. Then historical argument: at the time of the Prophet, there were only three categories: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. If Muslims are a fourth category, not mentioned, then they must be either believers or disbelievers. If they are believers, then the distinction collapses; if they are disbelievers, then their islam would not be accepted because only islam is accepted, but they would be disbelievers. Thus the claim leads to manifest disbelief. The author concludes with 'والله الموفق' (Allah is the Grantor of success).

الإسلام
الهداية
المسلمون

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think iman and islam are distinct based on the Hadith of Jibril, where the Prophet defines islam, iman, and ihsan separately.
Correction: This passage shows that in the Quran and other hadiths, the terms are used interchangeably, and the distinction in the Hadith of Jibril is not a categorical separation but a pedagogical explanation.

?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

Logical and Historical Refutation of the Distinction
The author presents logical and historical arguments to prove iman and islam are identical, including a reductio ad absurdum and the absence of a fourth category.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and historical arguments that refute the claim that iman and islam are distinct, and see how the distinction leads to absurdity.

Core Idea
Separating iman and islam leads to logical contradictions and contradicts Quranic categories.

After presenting scriptural proofs, the author strengthens his case with logical reasoning and historical evidence. He argues that if iman and islam were distinct, the Quran's division of people into two groups would leave no place for Muslims, and the historical reality of the Prophet's time shows only three categories. This lesson unpacks these powerful arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the argument from Quranic division
The author points out that Allah divides creation into believers and disbelievers (Quran 64:2) and talks of faces turning white and black (Quran 3:106). If Muslims were a separate category, they would be left out.
Ask yourself: which group would Muslims belong to in these verses?
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
If iman and islam are distinct, then one could exist without the other. But in this world and the Hereafter, no rulings distinguish a 'believer who is not a Muslim' from a 'Muslim who is not a believer'. This shows the distinction is meaningless.
The author uses conditional reasoning: if distinct, then there should be separate rulings; there are none, so the claim is false.
3
Apply the historical argument
At the time of the Prophet, people were only three types: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite. If Muslims were a fourth, they would have been mentioned. Since they are not, Muslims must be believers. If they were disbelievers, their Islam would be rejected.
This argument appeals to the absence of a fourth category in the Quran and history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكِتَابَ وَالْأُمِّينَ أَسْلَمْتُمْ فَإِنْ أَسْلَمُوا فَقَدِ اهْتَدَوا جعلهم في هذه الآية مهتدين بإسلامهم كما جعلهم في الآية الأولى مهتدين بإيمانهم، فهذا دليل واضح لا شك فيه أن جعل الإيمان والإسلام شيئًا واحدا لا يفترقان، وقال يوسف عليه السلام: تَوَفَّنِي مُسلِمًا وَالْحِقْنِي بِالصَّلِحِينَ وغير المؤمن لا يلحق بالصالحين وقال تعالى: يَمُنُّونَ عَلَيْكَ أَنْ أَسْلَمُوا قُل لَّا تَمُنُّوا عَلَى إِسْلَامَكُم بَلِ اللَّهُ يَمُنُّ عَلَيْكُمْ أَنْ هَدَنَكُمْ لِلْإِيمَنِ إِن كُنتُمْ صدِقِينَ وقد روى عن النبي عليه السلام أنه قال: "لا يدخل الجنة إلا نفس مؤمنة وروى إلا نفس مسلمة، ثم لا تنازع في جميع المسلمين أن الدار التي الأهل الإسلام هي لأهل الإيمان وأن التي هي لهؤلاء، فهي لهؤلاء وكذا الله تعالى قسم الخلق فقال: فَمِنكُمْ كَافِرٌ وَمِنكُم مُّؤْمِنٌ وقال : يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوهٌ فما فتوى صاحب هذا القول في المسلم أنه من أي قسم في الآيتين، ثم يقال له لو كان الاسمان اسمين لمتغايرين لتصور وجود أحدهما بدون الآخر ولتصور مؤمن ليس بمسلم ومسلم ليس بمؤمن ثم لو كان كذلك فما قولك في مؤمن ليس بمسلم أو مسلم ليس بمؤمن في أحكام الدنيا والآخرة؟ فإن ثبت لأحدهما حكمًا ليس للآخر ظهر ضلالة، وإن لم يثبت ظهر بطلان قوله، ثم الناس في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كانوا على ثلاثة أصناف مؤمن وكافر ومنافق فمن أيهم كان المسلم إذ لم يكن فيهم رابع؟ فإن قالوا: كان من المؤمنين تركوا مذهبهم وإن قالوا كان من الكافرين ينبغي أن لا يقبل إلا ذلك الدين وهو الكفر أو النفاق بقوله : ( وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ ) والإيمان غيره فلا يقبل بل يقبل إما الكفر وإما النفاق والقول به كفر ظاهر، والله الموفق.
The Book and the unlettered, have you submitted? If they submit then they are guided. He made them in this verse guided by their submission (islam) just as He made them in the first verse guided by their faith (iman). So this is clear evidence, no doubt in it, that He made iman and islam one thing that do not separate. And Yusuf peace be upon him said: 'Cause me to die as a Muslim and join me with the righteous.' And the non-believer is not joined with the righteous. And He said Most High: 'They consider it a favor to you that they have submitted. Say: Do not consider your submission a favor to me; rather Allah confers favor upon you that He has guided you to faith, if you are truthful.' And it was narrated from the Prophet peace be upon him that he said: 'None shall enter Paradise except a believing soul' and it was narrated 'except a Muslim soul'. Then there is no dispute among all Muslims that the abode whose people are Islam is for the people of faith, and that which is for these is for those. Similarly, Allah Most High divided creation and said: 'Among you are disbelievers and among you are believers.' And He said: 'On the day when faces become white and faces become black.' So what is the verdict of the proponent of this view concerning the Muslim: from which group is he in the two verses? Then it is said to him: If the two names were two distinct names, it would be conceivable for one to exist without the other, and it would be conceivable for a believer not to be a Muslim and a Muslim not to be a believer. Then if that were so, what do you say about a believer who is not a Muslim or a Muslim who is not a believer regarding the rulings of this world and the Hereafter? If a ruling is established for one that is not for the other, his error becomes apparent; and if it is not established, the invalidity of his statement becomes apparent. Then the people at the time of the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him were of three types: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite. From which of them was the Muslim, since there was no fourth? If they say: He was among the believers, they abandon their position; if they say he was among the disbelievers, then no religion should be accepted except that religion, which is disbelief or hypocrisy, by His saying: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him.' And iman is other than it, so it would not be accepted; rather either disbelief or hypocrisy is accepted. And this statement is manifest disbelief. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1103

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument for the identity of iman and islam, using Quranic verses, a prophetic hadith, and logical reasoning. The author begins by citing Quran 3:20 where Allah says to the People of the Book and the unlettered: 'If they submit (aslamu) then they are guided.' The author notes that in this verse guidance is linked to submission (islam), just as in another verse guidance is linked to faith (iman). This shows that iman and islam are the same. Then the author cites the Prophet Yusuf's prayer to die as a Muslim, arguing that only a believer is joined with the righteous, implying that islam equals iman. Next, Quran 49:17 is quoted, where the Bedouins think their submission (islam) is a favor, but Allah says He guided them to faith (iman). This shows that islam leads to iman, but the verse treats them as essentially the same in context. Then a hadith is cited: 'None shall enter Paradise except a believing soul' and also narrated as 'except a Muslim soul', indicating interchangeable usage. Then the author argues that there is no dispute among Muslims that Paradise is for Muslims, which is also for believers. Also, Quran 64:2 divides people into disbelievers and believers, not a separate category for Muslims. Similarly, Quran 3:106 speaks of faces turning white and black, implying two groups only. So the proponent of the distinction is asked: which group does the Muslim belong to? Then a reductio ad absurdum is presented: if iman and islam are distinct, it should be possible for a believer to not be a Muslim and vice versa, but in the rulings of this world and the Hereafter, no distinction is made. Then historical argument: at the time of the Prophet, there were only three categories: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. If Muslims are a fourth category, not mentioned, then they must be either believers or disbelievers. If they are believers, then the distinction collapses; if they are disbelievers, then their islam would not be accepted because only islam is accepted, but they would be disbelievers. Thus the claim leads to manifest disbelief. The author concludes with 'والله الموفق' (Allah is the Grantor of success).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that iman and islam are different, and a person can be a Muslim without having iman in the heart.
Correction: This passage demonstrates that in the Quran and in practice, no such distinction exists; the categories of believer and disbeliever are exhaustive, and the historical reality of the Prophet's time confirms that Muslims were considered believers.

Refutation of Distinguishing Islam from Iman: The Verse of the Bedouins
Refutation of a theological distinction using Qur'an and Hadith interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that Islam and Iman are distinct by interpreting the verse of the Bedouins and initiating the argument from the Hadith of Jibril.

Core Idea
Outward submission without inner faith is not true Islam.

Some argue that Islam and Iman are separate because the Quran and Hadith mention them in different contexts. The author tackles this by first explaining the verse where the Bedouins say 'We believe' and are corrected to say 'We submit.' He shows that this submission is not the true Islam of religion but mere fear, not a proof of separation. The passage then begins the parallel argument from the Hadith of Jibril, though it cuts off.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author addresses two proofs: the verse and the hadith.
The passage is incomplete at the end.
2
Understand the opponents' argument from the verse
Opponents use verse 49:14 to claim that islam without iman is possible. Identify how they argue that the Bedouins were told to say 'we submitted' not 'we believed'.
3
See the author's explanation
The author explains that 'استسلمنا' here means submission out of fear, not the true Islam that is the religion of Allah. This is key to the refutation.
4
Recognize the absurd consequence
If outward submission without faith were accepted as true Islam, then hypocrites would be considered Muslims, which is false.
This shows the corruption of the opponents' interpretation.
5
Begin the Hadith argument
The author then turns to the Hadith of Jibril and argues that if Islam and Iman are truly distinct, one should be able to exist without the other. The argument cuts off here.
The lesson only covers the start of this second argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على من قال : إن الإسلام غير الإيمان والجواب عن تعلقهم بالآية قلنا: معناها - والله أعلم - أي: قولوا استسلمنا خوفًا من معرة السيف لا أن المراد منه حقيقة الإسلام الذي مراد بقوله تعالى: وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ إذ لو كان كذلك والآية في المنافقين وكان الإسلام عندهم هو الأمور الظاهرة التي ذكرت في خبر جبريل عليه السلام، وقد انقاد أهل النفاق لهذا وقبلوها لكان ينبغي أن لا يقبل إلا ذلك، ولا يقبل إيمان المخلص ويقبل ذلك من أهل النفاق، ودخلوا تحت وعد المسلمين وإن لم يكن الإيمان دخل قلوبهم وهذا ظاهر الفساد، والله الموفق. وهذا هو الجواب عن تعلقهم بحديث جبريل عليه السلام وهو أن نقول لهم: إذا كان الإسلام غير الإيمان لابد أن يتصور وجود أحدهما حال عدم الآخر على ما هو حقيقة المغايرة، ثم لو أن إنسانًا أتى بجميع ما ذكر النبي عليه السلام في جواب قوله : ما الإسلام؟ وامتنع عن اكتساب ما ذكره عليه السلام في جواب قوله
The response to those who say that Islam is other than Iman: The answer to their attachment to the verse (49:14): We say: Its meaning – and Allah knows best – is: Say we have submitted out of fear of the harm of the sword, not that the intended meaning is the reality of Islam which is intended by His saying Most High: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him.' For if that were the case, and the verse is about the hypocrites, and Islam according to them is the outward matters mentioned in the report of Jibril peace be upon him, and the people of hypocrisy complied with this and accepted it, then it would be appropriate that only that (outward islam) be accepted, and the sincere believer's iman would not be accepted, and that (outward islam) would be accepted from the people of hypocrisy, and they would fall under the promise of Muslims even though iman did not enter their hearts. And this is manifest corruption. And Allah is the Grantor of success. And this is the answer to their attachment to the hadith of Jibril peace be upon him: we say to them: If Islam is other than iman, it must be conceivable for one to exist in the absence of the other, as is the reality of distinction. Then if a person performs all that the Prophet peace be upon him mentioned in answer to his question 'What is Islam?' and refrains from acquiring what he mentioned peace be upon him in answer to his question...
Source pages p. 1104

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Islam is distinct from Iman. The author first addresses the opponents' proof from the Quranic verse in Al-Hujurat (49:14) where the Bedouins say 'We believe' and Allah says 'Say: You have not believed; rather say: We have submitted.' The opponents argue that this shows submission (islam) without faith (iman) is possible. The author explains that the verse refers to hypocrites who merely verbally submitted out of fear, not sincere islam. Therefore, 'استسلمنا' means 'we have submitted' in the sense of outward compliance, not the true islam that is the religion of Allah. If it were true islam, then the hypocrites would be accepted as Muslims, but they are not because they lack iman. Then the author turns to the hadith of Jibril, where the Prophet defined islam, iman, and ihsan separately. The opponents use this to claim distinction. The author argues that if islam and iman are truly distinct, then it should be conceivable for one to exist without the other. Then he puts forward a scenario: if a person does all the outward acts of islam (prayer, zakat, etc.) but does not acquire iman (inner belief), what is his status? The author leaves the argument unfinished in this passage, but the implication is that such a person would not be a true believer, and thus islam without iman is not accepted. The passage emphasizes that the distinction leads to absurdities.

حقيقة الإسلام
خبر جبريل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the verse (49:14) proves that a person can be a Muslim without having iman in the heart.
Correction: The verse refers to hypocrites who submitted out of fear, not true Islam. True Islam always includes iman, as the verse later emphasizes that the religion accepted by Allah is only Islam.

Key Takeaway
True Islam and Iman are inseparable; outward acts without inner belief are not accepted as genuine Islam.

The Muslim is Not Separate from the Believer
The author argues against separating Muslim from believer using historical and logical reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that a Muslim cannot be a separate category from believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite, and why this refutes the claim that Islam and faith are separable.

Core Idea
The Prophet's community had only three categories: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite.

In this passage, the author tackles a claim that a Muslim might be distinct from a believer. He uses a simple but powerful historical argument: at the time of the Prophet, people were divided into only three groups—believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites. There was no fourth group of 'Muslims' separate from these. This forces the claimant to either abandon their position or accept a clearly false conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a question and then a dilemma.
2
Identify the initial dilemma
The author begins by asking: if a Muslim is not a believer, do they have different rulings? If a different ruling exists, error appears; if not, the claim is false.
This sets up the logical framework.
3
Understand the historical premise
The author states that in the Prophet's time, there were only three categories: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. There was no fourth 'Muslim' category.
This is a key factual premise.
4
Follow the two options
If the claimant says the Muslim was a believer, they abandon their own doctrine. If they say the Muslim was a disbeliever, then only disbelief or hypocrisy would be acceptable, which is contradicted by Qur'an 3:85.
The verse states that only Islam is accepted.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that the position that Muslim is separate from believer leads to clear disbelief. Understand why this is a strong refutation.
Consider how this argument protects the unity of Islam and faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو مسلم ليس بمؤمن في أحكام الدنيا والآخرة؟ فإن ثبت لأحدهما حكمًا ليس للآخر ظهر ضلالة، وإن لم يثبت ظهر بطلان قوله، ثم الناس في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كانوا على ثلاثة أصناف مؤمن وكافر ومنافق فمن أيهم كان المسلم إذ لم يكن فيهم رابع؟ فإن قالوا: كان من المؤمنين تركوا مذهبهم وإن قالوا كان من الكافرين ينبغي أن لا يقبل إلا ذلك الدين وهو الكفر أو النفاق بقوله : ( وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ منه ) والإيمان غيره فلا يقبل بل يقبل إما الكفر وإما النفاق والقول به كفر ظاهر، والله الموفق.
Or a Muslim who is not a believer in the rulings of this world and the Hereafter? If a ruling is established for one of them that is not for the other, his error appears, and if it is not established, the falsity of his statement appears. Then people in the time of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, were of three types: a believer, a disbeliever, and a hypocrite. Which of them was the Muslim since there was no fourth among them? If they say: he was from the believers, they abandon their doctrine; if they say he was from the disbelievers, then only that religion should be accepted, which is disbelief or hypocrisy according to His statement: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will not be accepted from him' (3:85). And faith is other than it, so it is not accepted; rather, either disbelief or hypocrisy is accepted, and saying that is clear disbelief. And God is the Grantor of success.

Commentary
This passage is an argument against those who claim that a Muslim is not a believer. The author begins by posing a dilemma: if the claimant asserts that a Muslim has a ruling in this world and the Hereafter that is different from a believer, then if such a ruling can be established, his error becomes apparent; if it cannot, his statement is false. Then the author uses a historical argument: at the time of the Prophet, people were only three categories: believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites. There was no fourth category of 'Muslim' distinct from these. So which category would the 'Muslim' belong to? If they say 'from the believers', they abandon their own doctrine that Islam and faith are separate. If they say 'from the disbelievers', then the only religion that should be accepted is disbelief or hypocrisy, because the verse (3:85) states that only Islam is accepted, and if Islam is different from faith, then faith would not be accepted; only disbelief or hypocrisy would be acceptable, which is clearly false. The author concludes that this position leads to clear disbelief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Muslim and believer are different categories; one can be a Muslim without being a believer.
Correction: The passage shows that in the Prophet's time, people were only believers, disbelievers, or hypocrites, so a Muslim must be one of these, and the only consistent identification is with believers.

Key Takeaway
The early Muslim community recognized only three categories, so a Muslim cannot be separate from a believer.

The Prophet's community had only three categories. If you are honest, which category describes your inner state right now? What action will you take to move from hypocrisy or complacency to true belief?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

The Verse on Seeking Another Religion: A Refutation
The author refutes the claim that Islam and faith are separate using the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quranic verse 'Whoever seeks a religion other than Islam' refers to hypocrites' outward submission, not to a separation between Islam and faith.

Core Idea
The verse condemns hypocritical submission, not true faith.

The author addresses a common misinterpretation of a key Quranic verse. Some argue that the verse implies Islam (outward submission) is different from faith (inner belief). But the author shows that the verse actually speaks about hypocrites who merely pretended to submit out of fear. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that the author is responding to a claim that Islam is not faith. Identify the verse referenced.
The verse is Quran 3:85.
2
Identify the author's main interpretation
The author says the verse means hypocrites said 'we submit' out of fear of the sword, not that it refers to true Islam. Locate this point.
3
Follow the logical reductio ad absurdum
The author argues: if the verse were about outward actions only, then hypocrites would be accepted and sincere believers might not be. This is clearly corrupt. Trace this reasoning.
This shows the absurdity of the opponent's view.
4
Conclude with the author's final judgment
The author declares the opposing interpretation as 'clearly corrupt.' Reflect on the importance of correct understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على من قال : إن الإسلام غير الإيمان والجواب عن تعلقهم بالآية قلنا: معناها - والله أعلم - أي: قولوا استسلمنا خوفًا من معرة السيف لا أن المراد منه حقيقة الإسلام الذي مراد بقوله تعالى: وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ إذ لو كان كذلك والآية في المنافقين وكان الإسلام عندهم هو الأمور الظاهرة التي ذكرت في خبر جبريل عليه السلام، وقد انقاد أهل النفاق لهذا وقبلوها لكان ينبغي أن لا يقبل إلا ذلك، ولا يقبل إيمان المخلص ويقبل ذلك من أهل النفاق، ودخلوا تحت وعد المسلمين وإن لم يكن الإيمان دخل قلوبهم وهذا ظاهر الفساد، والله الموفق.
The response to those who say that Islam is not faith. And the answer to their clinging to the verse: we said: its meaning—and God knows best—is: say 'we have submitted' out of fear of the harm of the sword, not that what is intended is the reality of Islam which is intended by His statement: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will not be accepted from him.' For if it were so, and the verse is about the hypocrites, and Islam according to them is the outward matters mentioned in the hadith of Gabriel, peace be upon him, and the people of hypocrisy submitted to this and accepted it, then only that should be accepted, and the faith of the sincere should not be accepted, and that should be accepted from the people of hypocrisy, and they would enter under the promise of the Muslims even though faith did not enter their hearts. This is clearly corrupt. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1104

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who use the Quranic verse 3:85 to argue that Islam is different from faith. The author explains the verse's meaning: when the hypocrites were told to say 'we submit', they meant outward submission out of fear of the sword, not the true Islam intended by the verse. If the verse were about hypocrites as they claim, and if Islam were merely outward actions (as the hadith of Gabriel mentions), then the hypocrites who outwardly performed these actions would be accepted, while the true believers who have faith in their hearts might not be. This leads to the absurd conclusion that hypocrites would be under the promise of the Muslims, even without faith in their hearts. The author declares this interpretation clearly corrupt.

Key Terms
إسلام
إيمان
نفاق
استسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Quran 3:85 shows that Islam (outward submission) is separate from faith (inner belief).
Correction: The author explains that the verse actually refers to hypocrites who outwardly submitted out of fear, not to true believers. True Islam includes both outward and inward aspects.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the verse 'Whoever seeks a religion other than Islam' primarily refer to?
A) True believers
B) Hypocrites who submitted outwardly
C) Disbelievers
D) All Muslims

Key Takeaway
The verse about seeking another religion refers to hypocrites' outward submission, not to a distinction between Islam and faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas in your life where you merely submit outwardly—going through the motions—while your heart is far from Allah? What is one specific action you do out of habit or fear rather than genuine faith?
?
When you read the Quran or perform salah, do you ever check your heart's intention? How can you ensure your submission is not merely out of fear of people's judgment?
?
If God were to judge you based only on your outward actions, would you be content? But He knows your inner state. What is one hidden attitude you need to repent of today?

Refutation Using the Hadith of Jibril
Author refutes the separation of Islam and Iman using a hypothetical and the hadith of Jibril.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that Islam and faith are distinct, using a logical hypothetical and the hadith of Jibril to expose contradictions.

Core Idea
Claiming Islam and Iman are separate leads to absurdities that contradict the Quran and common sense.

The author tackles the opponents' use of the hadith of Gabriel to argue that Islam and faith are separate. He first establishes the logical criterion for distinctness, then presents a powerful hypothetical: if a person performs all the acts of Islam but refuses the acts of faith, what is his status? Both possible answers lead to contradictions—either with the Quranic description of hypocrites or with the basic link between action and identity. The author then addresses the proper understanding of the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the literal translation to grasp the argument.
The passage is a single continuous refutation.
2
Understand the logical criterion
Notice how the author begins: if two things are distinct, one must be conceivable without the other. This is the foundation of his argument.
3
Follow the hypothetical scenario
The author imagines a person who does all the acts of Islam but not the acts of faith. Then ask: what is his status?
This is the key test.
4
Observe the refutation of both answers
The author shows that saying 'yes' (he is a saved Muslim) contradicts the Quran on hypocrites, while saying 'no' violates the principle that actions define identity. Both are absurd.
This demonstrates the impossibility of the distinctness claim.
5
See the conclusion about the hadith
When asked for the meaning of the hadith, the author declines to interpret it himself, instead pointing to an authentic narration where the Prophet mentions only the pillars of Islam in the second question.
This undercuts the opponents' proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا هو الجواب عن تعلقهم بحديث جبريل عليه السلام وهو أن نقول لهم: إذا كان الإسلام غير الإيمان لابد أن يتصور وجود أحدهما حال عدم الآخر على ما هو حقيقة المغايرة، ثم لو أن إنسانًا أتى بجميع ما ذكر النبي عليه السلام في جواب قوله : ما الإسلام؟ وامتنع عن اكتساب ما ذكره عليه السلام في جواب قوله ما الإيمان؟ أيكون مسلماً ينجو عما ينجو به المسلمون في الآخرة وينال به ما للمسلمين في الآخرة؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، فقد جعلوا المكذب بقلبه الجاحد بجميع ما يجب تصديقه بالقلب مسلمًا فائزاً بالخلود في الجنة ناجيًا من العذاب، مع أن الله تعالى أخبر أن المنافقين فى الدرك الأسفل من النار وهذا ظاهر البطلان، وإن قالوا: لا. قيل : ولم وقد أتى بما هو الإسلام؟ وكيف يتصور أن يأتي شخص بما هو الإسلام ولا يكون مسلما ؟ أفيجوز أن يأتي شخص بالقعود ولا يكون قاعدًا، وكذا هذا الأكل والشرب والمشي وغير ذلك من الأفعال الحسية، وكذا من الطاعة والمعصية والإيمان والكفر والصوم والصلاة وهذا إنكار الحقائق، فإن قالوا: فما معنى الحديث؟ قلنا: لسنا بأولى بالاشتغال ببيان معنى الحديث منكم، إنما علينا إبطال كلامكم وإفساد احتجاجكم به، وقد قلنا بحمد الله تعالى ثم نقول: ذكر في الروايات الصحيحة أنه سأل في المرة الثانية عن شرائع الإسلام، وقال النبي عليه السلام: أقام الصلاة وإيتاء الزكاة وصوم رمضان وحج البيت هكذا أخبرنا الشيخ المعدل أبو محمد عبد الله بن محمد المعدل النسفي عن الشيخ الخطيب أبي العباس جعفر بن محمد بن المستغفري النسفي الخطيب بها ، وكانت له عناية بليغة في باب علم الأخبار بإسناد متصل عن أبي حنيفة عن علقمة بن مرثد عن ابن عمر - رضي الله عنهما - الحديث بطوله، وكان فيه على نحو ما بينا، وهكذا
And this is the answer to their clinging to the hadith of Gabriel, peace be upon him. And it is that we say to them: if Islam is other than faith, it is necessary that the existence of one can be conceived in the absence of the other, as is the reality of distinctness. Then if a person were to perform all that the Prophet, peace be upon him, mentioned in answer to his question 'What is Islam?' and refrained from acquiring what he mentioned in answer to his question 'What is faith?', would he be a Muslim who is saved from what the Muslims are saved from in the Hereafter and attains what the Muslims attain in the Hereafter? If they say: yes, then they have made a person who denies in his heart, who rejects all that must be believed in the heart, a Muslim who succeeds to eternal paradise and is saved from punishment, despite God Almighty informing that the hypocrites are in the lowest depths of Hellfire. This is clearly false. And if they say: no, it is said: why, when he has performed what is Islam? And how can it be conceived that a person performs what is Islam and is not a Muslim? Is it permissible for a person to perform sitting and not be sitting? And likewise eating, drinking, walking, and other sensory actions, and likewise obedience and disobedience, faith and disbelief, fasting and prayer? This is a denial of realities. If they say: what then is the meaning of the hadith? We say: we are not more entitled to engage in explaining the meaning of the hadith than you. Rather, we are obligated to nullify your statement and refute your argument with it. And we have said, praise be to God, then we say: it is mentioned in the authentic narrations that he asked in the second time about the laws of Islam, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'establishing prayer, giving zakat, fasting Ramadan, and pilgrimage to the House.' Thus informed us the trustworthy teacher Abu Muhammad Abdullah ibn Muhammad al-Mu'addal al-Nasafi from the preacher Abu al-Abbas Ja'far ibn Muhammad ibn al-Mustaghfiri al-Nasafi, the preacher there, who had a great concern for the science of hadith, with a connected chain from Abu Hanifa from Alqama ibn Marthad from Ibn Umar, may God be pleased with them both, the hadith in its entirety, and it contained what we have explained. And so on.
Source pages p. 1104

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the argument that the hadith of Gabriel proves a separation between Islam and faith. The author first establishes the logical requirement of distinctness: if two things are truly different, one can exist without the other. Then he presents a hypothetical: a person performs all the acts of Islam (prayer, zakat, fasting, pilgrimage) but refuses to perform the acts of faith (belief in the heart). If the opponents say such a person is a Muslim saved in the Hereafter, then they are effectively saying that a person who rejects all belief in the heart is a Muslim destined for paradise, contradicting the Quranic verse that hypocrites are in the lowest depths of Hell. If they say he is not saved, then they must explain how one can perform Islam and not be a Muslim, which is like saying one can sit without being seated—an absurd denial of realities. When asked for the meaning of the hadith, the author states his task is not to interpret but to refute their misuse of it. He then reports an authentic narration where the Prophet, in the second question, specified the pillars of Islam (prayer, zakat, fasting, pilgrimage), indicating that these are the outward practices of Islam. The author concludes that the hadith does not support their claim.

Key Terms
حديث جبريل
إسلام
إيمان
مغايرة
نفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith of Jibril proves that Islam and Iman are completely separate and independent entities.
Correction: The author shows that logical consequences of full separation lead to absurdities, and the hadith itself, when examined properly, does not support total separation.

Checkpoint
According to the author, if someone performs all the acts of Islam but none of the acts of faith, what is the status of that person?
A) He is a Muslim saved from Hell.
B) He is a hypocrite in the lowest depth of Hell.
C) The hadith does not address this scenario.
D) The author does not give a direct answer.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Jibril does not prove a separation between Islam and Iman; claiming it does leads to contradictions with the Quran and logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite the shahada and perform the prayers, but do you ever examine your heart to see if it truly affirms what your tongue says? If your inner faith is weak or absent, are you not exactly the person the author describes—doing Islam without being a Muslim? What will you do today to align your heart with your actions?
?
The author argues that performing Islam without Iman is as absurd as sitting without being seated. Yet how many of your prayers are performed without presence of heart? Will you commit to spending even five minutes before each prayer to renew your intention and focus your mind on what you are saying?
?
When you hear the hadith of Jibril, do you take it as permission to separate 'Islamic practice' from 'faith'? If so, how would you answer the author's challenge? Can you honestly say your understanding of the hadith does not lead to the contradictions he points out? If not, what change must you make in how you understand your own deen?

Metaphorical Use of Iman for Sharia
The author explains that 'iman' is used metaphorically for the sharia, citing Quran 2:143.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the term 'iman' in the Quran can be used metaphorically to refer to the entire body of religious practices, not just internal belief.

Core Idea
'Iman' in the Quran sometimes means the sharia itself.

This brief passage from the text clarifies a key linguistic and theological point: when the Quran uses the word 'iman', it does not always refer solely to faith in the heart. In some contexts, it encompasses the outward acts of worship. The author cites the well-known verse about prayer to illustrate this metaphorical usage. Understanding this helps students of theology and exegesis avoid a narrow interpretation of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style of the matn.
2
Identify the key claim
The author states that 'iman' is used metaphorically (majaz) for the sharia. Find the phrase 'بطريق المجاز' and understand its significance.
This is a common rhetorical device in Quranic language.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites Quran 2:143 ('And Allah would not let your faith go to waste') where 'iman' refers to prayer. Reflect on how this verse supports the metaphorical usage.
This verse was revealed regarding the change of qibla.
4
Connect to a common misunderstanding
Some assume 'iman' always means only belief. This passage shows it can include actions. Consider why this distinction matters for theology.
This impacts discussions on the relationship between faith and works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأورد به الشرائع بطريق المجاز كما يذكر الإيمان ويراد به الشرائع كالصلاة ونحوها على ما ذكرنا في قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَا كَانَ اللَّهُ لِيُضِيعَ إِيمَانَكُمْ ﴾، والله الموفق.
And he brought the religious laws by way of metaphor, just as 'iman' is mentioned and what is meant is the religious laws, like prayer and similar things, as we mentioned in His statement, the Exalted: 'And Allah would not let your faith go to waste' (2:143), and Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1108

Commentary
This passage is a brief definitional note. The author clarifies a linguistic point: the word 'iman' (faith) is sometimes used metaphorically to refer to the entire body of religious laws (shara'i'), as seen in the verse where 'iman' means the prayer. This is a key exegetical point to understand the Quranic usage.

Key Terms
إيمان
شرائع
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'iman' only means belief in the heart and never refers to actions.
Correction: The passage shows that 'iman' is used metaphorically for the sharia, which includes actions like prayer, indicating that in Quranic usage it can encompass outward practices.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the term 'iman' used in the Quran?
A) Only for belief
B) Metaphorically for the sharia
C) Only for prayer
D) As a synonym for sharia

Key Takeaway
The Quranic term 'iman' can refer metaphorically to the entire set of religious laws, not just inner faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite Surah Al-Baqarah 2:143, do you simply assume 'iman' means 'faith' without considering the context? Today, you learned that it actually refers to salah. How will you ensure that you, from now on, pause to reflect on the deeper meanings of Quranic words before forming an understanding? Write one specific action you will take.
?
This lesson shows that a single term in the Quran can shift in meaning based on the context. How often do you read verses superficially, missing the layers of meaning? What is one verse you commonly recite that you might have misunderstood? Commit to looking up its tafsir this week to uncover its intended meaning.
?
If 'iman' can encompass action, how does that challenge your personal definition of faith? Are you one who treats belief as a mental state separate from daily practice, or do you see your prayers, charity, and other acts as essential expressions of your iman? Starting tomorrow, choose one religious act and perform it with the conscious intention that it is part of your faith.
